Showing Concern for the Soldiers on the Front Line, All Parties Extend Solace and Encouragement, Saving on Food and Clothing to Enthusiastically Donate Funds, Sharing the Same Hatred of the Enemy and Boosting Morale 9

(Beiping) The aid-to-Suiyuan movement in the Peiping educational community is proceeding actively. Faculty and staff of various universities donated one day's salary, which was separately remitted to Suiyuan. The Peiping-Tianjin Educational Federation held a meeting today to decide on aid-to-Suiyuan measures. Fundraising measures by Peiping student groups have been decided, and the five drawbacks considered by the local authorities will be avoided by the group. The aid-to-Suiyuan association of the Normal University was established and decided on measures such as saving food, stopping fires, and fundraising. Fundraising in primary and secondary schools also started today. The municipal authorities invited the principals of various universities tonight to exchange views on issues such as academic aid to Suiyuan and maintaining order in Peiping. The Peiping-Tianjin Educational Federation held an ad hoc meeting today and resolved to donate 1,000 yuan in national currency, and publicly appointed Yang Zhikui, Zhou Binglin, and Mou Mo to go to Suidong to comfort the soldiers. (19th Special Telegram)

(Nanjing) The city's women's community, in order to comfort the soldiers fighting afar, sent a telegram to Fu and the soldiers on the front line, and established a fundraising committee, with Li Dequan as the chief captain, and Zhang Mojun, and others as captains of the first to tenth teams. The association received 400 towels donated by He Xiangning on the 19th. All faculty, staff and workers of the Nanjing Normal School donated one day's income and decided that all faculty, staff, and students would be vegetarian for one week and donate the savings. All employees of the Mongolian Committee initiated the donation of one day's income to the country. All faculty, staff, students, and workers of Nanjing No. 1 Middle School telegraphed Fu to collect one day's income to purchase winter clothes for the soldiers. The students of Nanjing Zhongying, Zhongnan, Dongfang, and Anhui Middle Schools temporarily ended their fundraising to assist the soldiers in Suiyuan on the 19th. Once detailed measures are decided, a general fundraising campaign will be launched again. The National Postal Workers' Union telegraphed its condolences to Fu Zuoyi and stipulated one-day contribution campaign measures, and issued orders to postal unions in various regions to urge members to enthusiastically donate, collect them, and remit them. All employees of the Jiangnan Automobile Company voluntarily donated one day's salary, amounting to one thousand four to five hundred yuan, as consolation money for the soldiers in Suiyuan, which will be remitted to Suiyuan upon collection. (19th Special Telegram)

(Xiamen) Support for Suiyuan among Xiamen citizens is becoming increasingly enthusiastic on the 19th. The Chamber of Commerce resolved to form a fundraising committee for the business community. On the spot, various trade associations donated 4,500 yuan, which was immediately remitted to Suiyuan. It was decided that from the 20th to the 24th, donations would be solicited from various businesses, banks, companies, wealthy merchants, and tycoons. On the 5th, all faculty and students of Xiamen University were divided into 30 teams and went to the towns and villages of Xiamen, He, and Gu to solicit donations. The principals of various middle schools held a joint meeting to proceed. Shops, residents, women, and children in the city automatically donated enthusiastically. More than 10,000 yuan was raised in two days, and the enthusiasm was unprecedented. In addition to donating 30,000 yuan for the purchase of machines, overseas Chinese merchant Li Pishu donated another 1,000 yuan to support Suiyuan. (19th Special Telegram)

(Zhenjiang) All sectors of Zhenjiang formed a committee on the 19th to comfort the soldiers in Suiyuan, with Leng Yuqiu as chairman, and divided into four groups: general affairs, communication, custody, and fundraising, to carry out fundraising and comfort activities. Two thousand yuan was immediately raised and remitted to the front, and a telegram was sent to Fu to encourage him. (19th Special Telegram)

(Tianjin) Primary schools in Tianjin have begun fundraising to comfort the soldiers in Suiyuan. Primary school students save on fruit and candy expenses and enthusiastically donate. (19th Special Telegram)

(Tianjin) On the 19th, students from various universities and colleges in Tianjin formed teams to solicit donations from the business community. The authorities, fearing accidental misunderstandings, dissuaded them from stopping. Various merchants will automatically express their views. (19th Special Telegram)

(Anqing) The Anhui Provincial Party Headquarters telegraphed Fu, Chairman of Suiyuan, and forwarded it to the soldiers on the front line, stating that Chahar and Suiyuan are the keys to the northern gate, and their gains and losses affect the overall situation. Recently, bandits and invaders have roamed around, wantonly invading, and all those with blood are indignant. Fortunately, you and the soldiers on the front line are fighting bravely and have repeatedly frustrated the enemy. The lower-ranking officials are listening and admire your heroism. I hope that you will be united and adhere to your original intentions, annihilate those ugly elements, and defend our border. The survival of the nation is deeply dependent on you. In addition to instructing the subordinates to actively raise funds to provide assistance, a special telegram is sent to express condolences, etc. In addition, faculty and staff of Anqing High School and Girls' Middle School donate their salaries, and students fast for one day, and the proceeds are remitted to the front. (19th Special Telegram)

(Anqing) The Anhui Provincial Journalists Association initiated a joint telegram to Chairman Fu and the soldiers on the front line by all people's organizations in the provincial capital, and all colleagues from various newspapers automatically initiated the donation of one day's income, which will be collected and submitted to the bank for remittance to Suiyuan to comfort the troops. (19th Special Telegram)

(Jiangyin) All officers and soldiers stationed in Jiangyin donated their one-day salary and saved on food on the 19th to assist the generals and soldiers who defended the country and suppressed bandits in Sui Province. The funds have been remitted. (19th Special Telegram)

(Fuzhou) All sectors here are enthusiastically donating to aid Suiyuan and plan to form a support association immediately to raise donations continuously. (19th Special Telegram)

(Hong Kong) The academic community in Hong Kong launched a fundraising campaign to comfort the soldiers in Sui. (19th Special Telegram)

(Taiyuan) The business community in Bing City decided to divide into twenty-two teams to solicit donations and comfort the troops. Prisoners in the prison fasted for one day today to save money and donate it. All parties are extremely excited and are preparing to donate as much as possible. The provincial government held a meeting today to discuss unified custody measures. (19th Special Telegram)

(Hangzhou) The Hangzhou City Secondary Above Schools Aid to Frontline Soldiers Conference telegraphed the National Government and the entire country, urging united and effective support, and expressing condolences to the soldiers on the front line. It was decided that all members would set out to solicit donations on the 21st and 22nd. (19th Special Telegram)

(Qingdao) The Qingdao academic and business communities have been donating funds and remitting them to Suiyuan for the past few days to comfort the soldiers suppressing the bandits. The remaining sectors will also jointly donate. (19th Special Telegram)

Song Zheyuan Discusses His Inspection Tour; He Had a Day-Long Meeting with Han Fuqu; The Situation in Suidong, Although Tense, is Not Worth Worrying About 10

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan met with reporters on the morning of the 19th and said that during this inspection tour, he passed through counties such as Gu'an, Renqiu, Hejian, and Nangong, inspected the stationed troops along the way, and inspected the administration of officials, cleaned up pending cases of banditry and drugs, and gave instructions on the policy direction of various counties. The autumn harvest in the whole province is still good, and the banditry has been suppressed, so the order is peaceful. When he was in Nangong, Chairman Han happened to be inspecting northern Shandong and arrived in Dezhou. Because they were very close, they had a day-long talk. He also told Han frankly about the general situation of Hebei and Chahar. Han gave a very detailed account of the situation of his visit to Chairman Chiang in Nanjing. In addition, there was also a general discussion on national affairs. Hebei and Shandong are adjacent to each other, and their situation is roughly the same. They should be on guard outside and appease inside under the overall national policy. Han completely agrees with this point. At 9:00 AM on the morning of the 18th, Han went east, and he also returned north. Because of the treasure problem, the various departments of the 29th Army will be redeployed. Although the situation in Suidong is tense, Chahar Province is still safe. The bandits who are attacking Sui are not worth worrying about. Because Inner Mongolia is cold and lacks food, it is very difficult in military terms, and the number of bandits is at most only ten thousand or so. With a rabble, it is difficult to last, so I hope that the people of the country will be calm. (19th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Beiping) When Song Zheyuan received visitors today, he expressed the opinion that the situation in Suiyuan would not turn serious because Japan did not admit any relationship with this incident. Therefore, the Chinese authorities can regard the invaders as bandits and disperse them. Song mentioned the meeting with Han Fuqu in Nangong on the 17th of this month, saying that they had discussed the situation in North China at that time for a long time. He said that Hebei and Shandong are adjacent, so they should help each other in the same boat and maintain law and order based on the principle of appeasing others internally and externally. The two completely agreed on this. (19th Reuters Telegram)

Economic Development in North China; Everything is Currently at a Standstill; The Japanese Military Is Not Very Interested; Li Sihao's Contact with the Japanese Side is Indefinite 11

(Tianjin) In order to develop the economy of North China, the Xingzhong Company planned to issue 20 million yuan in corporate bonds because there were no results in domestic fundraising, and wanted to invest in the Jingxing Mine. The Japanese military headquarters in Tianjin did not agree with this, and the two sides were in dispute. The Sui-KOU incident occurred, affecting the Japanese military headquarters' plan for economic investment in North China. Recently, except for navigation, everything has been at a standstill. Although Li Sihao has returned north, the contact with Staff Officer Ikeda is still indefinite. The attitude of the Japanese military headquarters in Tianjin is now indifferent and will reorganize the steps after the Sui incident unfolds. Osaka Kyodo Paper Manufacturing Co. plans to invest 5 million yuan and jointly set up a paper mill with Toyo Paper Manufacturing Co. in Tianjin. Recently, Chairman Oda Manzo has arrived in Tianjin to discuss the purchase of factory land. (19th Special Telegram)

Cheng Guorui and Others Secretly Plot Activities 12

(Tianjin) In a certain Tianjin concession, a frustrated former Zhili-Lu warlord planned to take advantage of the situation in Suiyuan-Eastern to disrupt public order. The authorities sent out many investigators. On the night of the 18th and the morning of the 19th, several accomplices were arrested in a certain inn in Hebei. The rest are being searched for. Cheng Guorui, the former Zhili-Lu army commander, and Wang Huchen, the pseudo-chief of staff, have secretly gone to the Xingtai and Lixian areas, attempting to gather old Zhili-Lu bandits and launch an uprising. The authorities have dispatched secret agents to follow them. According to officials in Tianjin, Cheng has been struggling in Changchun in recent years, lacking food and clothing, and no one in the puppet regime pays attention to him. Now he wants to find a way out in the political and military circles of North China, so he makes empty threats to intimidate the authorities. The defense within the Hebei-Chahar border is tight, and he will not be allowed to succeed. (19th Dispatch)

Jingxing Coal Mine Thriving 13

(Baoding) After reorganization, the Jingxing Coal Mine's 14th business year ended at the end of September, with a profit of 880,000, more than four times the previous years. The average daily output of coal is now 3,000 tons. Due to lack of transportation, there are 100,000 tons of coal in stock, which cannot be sold. If it cannot be transported out in another ten days, part of the work must be stopped, and at least 2,000 workers will lose their jobs. Director Gu Zhongxi is scheduled to attend Feng Zhi'an's inauguration ceremony on the 20th, then go to Beiping to meet with Song Zheyuan, asking him to find a way to allocate vehicles from the Beining Railway to help. According to Gu, the mine has built a wide-gauge railway, which will connect with the Zhengtai Railway at the end of December. Large hoists will be used and installed in January next year, trial operations will begin in February, and implementation will begin in March. It is estimated that the daily coal output can be increased to 5,000 tons. At the current coal price, the net sale is 4.3 yuan, and the estimated profit for the next year can reach more than 1 million. The Cixian mine has started construction and will be able to produce coal next month. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Pingyu Smuggling Seized 14

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 19th, when Pingyu Train No. 41 arrived in Tianjin from Beiping, it was carrying 20 pieces of smuggled rayon, which were seized by personnel stationed at the Xinzhan Customs. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Smuggled kerosene, totaling 3,000 boxes, was transported into Tianjin two weeks ago, and sales are extremely brisk, currently out of stock, and the price per box has increased to 7.3 yuan. The Tianjin Customs is working hard to intercept smuggled goods. The water patrol boat at the Dabai Bridge on the waterway has been quite effective. Most of the smuggled goods have been changed to be transported out by land, and those transported out along the Zunhua River are gradually decreasing. (19th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The General Inspectorate of Hebei-Chahar has been closed and all internal personnel have been dismissed. The original inspection team of fifty soldiers will be reorganized as ordered by the Political Council. (19th Dispatch)

Travel Correspondence

Flying from Shanghai to Xijing (Continued) 15

— Geng Ya

That day, the plane briefly stopped at Nanjing Ming Palace Airfield, having a hearty "foreign snack"—more than twenty barrels of gasoline. Then, it once again "chugged, chugged, chugged" and sang the song of "A Grand Journey of Ten Thousand Miles," raising its head and soaring into the sky, bravely advancing westward.

Among the passengers traveling in the sky this time was He Jiwu, who was about to take office as a member of the Guizhou Provincial Committee. When the China National Aviation Corporation was first founded in 1930, he served as its first general manager. In the aviation industry, he can be called an "old hand," and in the company, he can be called the founder. He said, "When China National Aviation Corporation first sold tickets, few people dared to buy them and ride. The first month's operating income was only 8,000 yuan; when he left the job the second year, it had just increased tenfold to 80,000 yuan. Now it has increased to more than 200,000 yuan, and new routes are still being extended gradually. This shows the progress of the Chinese people's understanding of air transportation and the development of the airline's business." I think the situation of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation is probably similar.

Generally speaking, to obtain safety when taking an airplane, one must have (1) a climate that helps success; (2) an aircraft with perfect mechanics; and (3) a pilot with pure skill. If conditions (1) and (2) are met, but the weather suddenly deteriorates halfway, encountering a storm and dark clouds, how to fly through the difficult situation will depend entirely on the pilot's skills and training. When a pilot is flying, because he has to take into account the airplane's ascent, descent, speed, climate, direction, and fuel level, his eyes, ears, hands, feet, and all his muscles, bones, and nerves must be mobilized, and he must persist without懈. For example, the first day of flying on the Shanghai-Kunming (Ming) line, from Shanghai to Chengdu, requires eight hours of work, which is really not something that an ordinary person can handle.

With the progress of modern science, various countries have repeatedly made new inventions, which have not only greatly contributed to human happiness but also encouraged the interest of scientists. It is said that aviation scholars are constantly researching and improving the mechanics of existing aircraft. For example, the takeoff and landing of airplanes requires large airfields, which is uneconomical and inconvenient. Therefore, some people are researching and improving it, wanting to change it from taking off and landing on a diagonal plane to a more vertical up and down. Or, they may even find a way to make the wings retractable, so that they can be used freely on land and in the air. If so, then a private individual with three to five acres of land can also prepare an airplane to play with. Although this is still an ideal, who knows if it will not become a reality in the future?

Just as the reporter removed the cotton stuffed in his ears (because he could not stand the noise of the engine, he had to use cotton to plug his ears) and was having a very interesting conversation with his companions, he only felt the fuselage tilt slightly, flying a circle with its wings at an angle, and then landed on the ground. Only then did he realize that he had arrived at the Wulibao Airfield in Zhengzhou, Henan. According to Huang Juechang, the telecommunications mechanic manager who was flying with the plane, "The climate in Zhengzhou is constantly changing. In the past, the flight would always sway a few times twenty minutes before arriving at the station; today, the sky is cloudy, (it was sunny in Jiangsu Province,) but it is so stable, it's really great!" Getting off the plane and walking, I saw that the grass in the airfield was withered and unbearable, compared with the green grass airfield in Longhua, Shanghai, it was like going from a temperate zone to a frigid zone. But the plains and fields seen along the way were similar to those in Jiangsu Province. The southbound plane that took off from Beiping at 7 a.m. had arrived ten minutes earlier and was covered with cloth, and would fly back north in two days.

The plane ate another big meal of gasoline, counted to be forty-seven empty barrels; after arriving in Xi'an, it ate another big meal. With such a large capacity, it is no wonder that it can carry heavy loads and travel far, flying ten thousand miles a day without showing any fatigue. It is a pity that it only eats Western food, and there are no domestic goods. The outflow of profits is secondary. If in an emergency, foreigners refuse to provide such a large amount of Western food, the strong man will not be able to "serve the public hungry", and he may not be able to avoid being sneered at by old oxcarts! It can be seen that saving the country through aviation is a matter of urgency, and saving the country through gasoline is also a matter of urgent importance. The best oil field in China is the Fushun field: but now "that bird has flown into someone else's cage", so we can only retreat and actively develop the two places of northern Shaanxi and Jiayuguan. It is hoped that the government will promote it first, and the industrialists will work hard later!

Looking down from the sky flying west from Zhengzhou, the Yellow River meanders below; Shouyang Mountain and Mount Hua rise and undulate to the south. On the border between Henan and Shaanxi, there are some low, flat hills, on the top of which are terraced fields chiseled full of circles, and the dwellings and cave dwellings are dug under the edge of the ground, only seeing scattered black holes in threes and fives, scattered east and west. Occasionally, a few maple trees stand beside the caves, which are indeed as the ancient poem says: "Frost leaves are redder than February flowers," needless to say, this has been embellished into a natural beautiful picture of autumnal desolation, evoking reverie. Later, I saw several cities in a row, the streets were all straight, and the houses were mostly "quadrangle courtyards". Their collective and new-style urban radial architecture were naturally very different; but a kind of strict and square feature was also very noticeable when looking from above. Especially Luoyang and Chang'an, who wouldn't say that they are old capitals with ancient charm, only enough to be used for mourning? But now they are gradually returning to youth! For example, since Luoyang established the Central Military Academy, everything has changed its old appearance; especially since Chairman Chiang has recently been stationed here, it has formed the center of politics. The new buildings in the city and the West Palace, as well as the newly built trees, can still be vaguely seen in the midst of the chilling autumn wind. Since Chang'an was designated as Xijing, it has worked hard on construction in recent years, and its achievements have made great progress, and its population has also increased to more than 200,000 (according to Lei Bao, the head of the Construction Department, the fixed population is 200,000, and there are about 50,000 mobile residents). It is even more imaginable that the future will become more prosperous.

Escaping a patch of clouds and fog, the plane seemed to be wiping against the shoulder of Mount Hua, flying low along the mountainside for a while. The telecommunications worker Huang Juechang came to ask us, "Do you want to eat Chinese or Western food in Xi'an? I'll telegraph the station to prepare it for you." Not long after, at 1 p.m., we arrived in Xi'an.

That day, I unintentionally ran into several friends. One was Tan Shiqin, whom I had seen in Qinghai before. He was sending a friend off on a plane at Nanjing Station. One was Xie ××, a patriot from Taiwan (now naturalized), whom I had seen several times during the January 28th Shanghai Incident. Now he and several comrades came to the Northwest for investigation. One was Ge Yuheng, the current director-general of the New Life Movement, whom I had known in Shenyang before the September 18th Incident. I had just seen a good room in the Xijing Guest House and turned around and ran into him. They were all thousands of miles away, and I had known them several years ago, and now we met by chance in the middle of the war. The changes in personnel are really inexplicable.

In the afternoon, they flew back to Changchun. Colonel Tanaka Ryukichi, a staff officer of the Kwantung Army, flew to Shangdu from Changchun on the 18th. Harada, a staff officer of the Kwantung Army, and Iijima, the commander of the air force brigade, also attended the meeting. After three hours of discussion, a response to the Suiyuan-Eastern incident has been decided. Harada and Iijima took the night train back to Changchun to report. (19th Dispatch)

Beijing-Shanghai Express Train Test Run Successful 21

(Nanjing) According to the results of the Beijing-Shanghai express train test run by the Two Routes Administration on the 19th, it can travel at 80 kilometers per hour and complete the entire Beijing-Shanghai route in four hours and twenty minutes. It is now set to a standard of four hours and thirty minutes. The methods are: 1. Stop at six stations along the route: Shangbei, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing. 2. There will be one express train each way every day, the northbound train leaving Shanghai at 8 a.m., and the southbound train leaving Beijing at 4 p.m. 3. Each train will have six first, second, and third class cars, without sleeper cars. 4. The fares will remain the same. 5. Passengers in each class will be assigned seats according to their tickets. Telephone reservations will be held until one minute before departure. According to the Ministry of Railways, the streamline-type new locomotives and passenger car bodies ordered by the Two Routes Administration from Britain have arrived in Shanghai and are being installed for express use. (19th Dispatch)

Sino-US Telephone Call Must Be Implemented Next Month 32

(Nanjing) The US side has replied and agreed to the Sino-US wireless Shanghai-New York call contract. The previous rumor that the call would be made on the 20th was inaccurate. It is now learned that the Sino-US sides have agreed on the Chinese time for the call to be from 10 p.m. to 12 p.m. every night, and the US time to be at noon during the day. The price is 21 US dollars per three minutes from Monday to Saturday (equivalent to 61 Chinese dollars), and 15 US dollars each time on Sunday. It will be implemented after all the procedures are ready. The call can be made around the 20th of next month. (19th Dispatch)

Execution for Drug Use to Be Implemented in January Next Year 33

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Committee for the Elimination of Opium and Drugs will be reorganized into the Nanjing Committee for the Prohibition of Opium and Drugs. A meeting will be held on the morning of the 21st to discuss the reorganization. The Provisional Regulations on the Punishment of Crimes Related to Opium and Drug Prohibition will be implemented from January next year. Anyone who commits drug use will be executed. Those who smoke opium will be sentenced to imprisonment for six months to two years. Those who relapse after quitting will be sentenced to imprisonment for one year to three years. Those who relapse after being ordered to quit will be sentenced to imprisonment for three years to ten years. Those who relapse three times will be executed. In order to implement the above regulations, the committee will also propose starting with earnest persuasion. (19th Dispatch)

Shanghai Business Representatives Visit Wu Dingchang 34

(Nanjing) The Shanghai National Goods Production and Sales Association and the Industrial Federation once gathered in Shanghai to discuss the methods of the National Goods Joint Business Company and sent Fang Yexian, Pan Yangyao, and others to Beijing to discuss everything. Fang and others arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 19th and went to the Ministry of Industry to see Minister Wu in the afternoon to discuss the methods of raising 2 million capital and preparing for it in major ports. They talked for two hours. It was generally decided that Fang and others would meet with Shanghai manufacturers again. It is reported that the existing national goods companies in various provinces and cities will also be strengthened. In the future, national goods joint business companies in Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Guangzhou, and other places will be established first, and then they will be promoted to the inland. It is said that it is very easy to establish the capital because the factories do not immediately receive cash when delivering goods. (19th Dispatch)

Allowances for Civil Servants Should Be Subject to Income Tax 35

(Nanjing) The Second Department of the Military Commission's Office believes that various allowances given to civil servants for rent, food, grooms, and travel expenses should be subject to income tax. It once sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance for explanation. It is now learned that the Ministry of Finance replied that the allowances are a kind of income from work and should be combined with the salary for taxation according to law. (19th Central News Agency)

When all the surcharges are reduced in 1939, the name of the surcharges will be corrected. The Executive Yuan has ordered the Henan Provincial Government to do so. Current Affairs Commentary

The Significance of America's Increased Defense in the Western Pacific 41

— Star

The Washington Naval Treaty and the London Naval Treaty, which maintained the balance of power in the Pacific, will expire at the end of this year. The arms race among the United States, Great Britain, and Japan in the Pacific has already begun. According to recent announcements by Washington military authorities, the United States intends to build air force bases on Midway Island and Wake Island. This would advance the United States' westernmost frontier in the Western Pacific by more than a thousand nautical miles from the Hawaiian Islands. The sensitive Japanese naval authorities are very uneasy. The American plan has very important implications for national defense and diplomacy. However, at present, the diplomatic significance seems to be more important than the defense significance.

The biggest weakness of American Pacific defenses is the lack of military bases. In the thousands of nautical miles of ocean between the Philippines and Hawaii, the United States does not have any important defensive positions. If an enemy of the United States were to attack the Philippines, the navy and air force stationed in Hawaii would certainly face the difficulty of "distant water not quenching immediate thirst." Fortunately, the development of aviation in recent years has provided military convenience to the United States. The speed of airplanes shortens the distance over the sea, and what the United States' hypothetical enemy fears most is air raids. Regular trans-Pacific flights from San Francisco to Hong Kong have already been realized. The shadow of American airplanes is often seen over the Western Pacific. Commercial airplanes can be converted into military ones at any time. If the air force bases on Wake Island and Midway Island are completed, the United States will have a greater chance of successfully defending the Philippines and conducting operations in the Far Eastern waters.

However, this American plan was triggered by Japan's declaration of the death of the Washington and London Naval Treaties. The current U.S. diplomatic policy is how to use various pressures to make Japan accept some of the principles of the various Washington treaties. Japan refuses to participate in the 1936 New Naval Treaty. Japan refuses to abide by the obligations of the Washington Nine-Power Treaty. Therefore, the only option is to use a large navy and air force policy to awaken Japan. Recently, former Secretary of State Stimson's book, "The Crisis in the Far East," severely criticized Japan's unilateral violation of the Nine-Power Treaty. He said that the United States agreed to Japan in 1922 not to establish military bases in the Western Pacific because Japan was willing to abide by the Nine-Power Treaty, respect China's sovereignty and independence, and maintain the open-door policy towards China. Now that Japan is destroying China's sovereignty and violating the open-door policy, the United States naturally has no obligation to remain undefended in the Pacific. Mr. Stimson further said that because the United States did not set up defenses in the Western Pacific and reduced its navy in accordance with Japan's naval power, it did not have the courage to make more concrete representations to Japan during the September 18th and January 28th incidents. The implication is self-evident.

We have always hoped that the great powers of the Pacific will seek peace again under the spirit of the 1922 treaty. Maintaining collective security in the Far East is better than any arms race or commercial competition. The Japanese side should realize that the motive for this American plan lies in diplomacy. If it becomes a reality, it is obviously very unfavorable to the Japanese Empire. The development of air power has reduced the role of Japan's superior naval ports and submarines in the Western Pacific. Moreover, the American and British Far East air routes have already been connected in Hong Kong. If the United States can borrow bases such as Hong Kong and Singapore in the South China Sea, and the United States has bases such as Wake Island, Midway Island, and Guam in the Western Pacific, the Japanese navy and air force will be surrounded. It is very difficult to restore the security after 1922.

The current arms race may only be a kind of active diplomatic expression. However, there is only a little over a month left in 1936. What will be the trend and result of the Pacific without a treaty is very obvious. China, the master of the western shore of the Pacific, cannot just stand by. It should actively strive for its final struggle for survival.

Content of the German-Japanese Alliance: Forming an Anti-Soviet Front; Germany Assists Japan in Reforming its Military 42

According to the North China Daily News, although both Tokyo and Berlin have remained silent regarding the rumored German-Japanese agreement, the North China Daily News has learned from reliable sources that its main features include a common anti-communist declaration and a signed treaty stipulating that Germany will sell war materials to Japan to enable it to reform its army within three or four years based on mechanization, and provide credit facilities to make this possible. Although Italy has been mentioned regarding the anti-communist front, it is said that although Italy is not involved in the political aspects of the agreement, it will endeavor to persuade Mussolini to join the joint anti-communist declaration in the future. It is heard that this declaration will clearly explain the seriousness of the harm of communism and that the West should unite to curb its spread, in view of the growing power of Soviet Russia in Europe and the Far East. The North China Daily News also learned that the military aspects of the agreement stipulate that Japan will purchase aircraft, tanks, and other war materials from Germany so that the Japanese army can be mechanized as soon as possible. It is said that after the recent large-scale exercises held by the Japanese army in Hokkaido, observers commented that the Japanese army showed weaknesses in mechanization. As a result, the Japanese military authorities formulated a reform program requiring 300 million yen. Germany now intends to shorten the Japanese reform program to three or four years, but this requires the assistance of Germany, because the Japanese deeply believe that Japan's domestic industry cannot meet this program and that there is still a huge surplus of military expenditures approved by the parliament that has not been absorbed by the military industry. It is heard that in order to help Japan purchase war materials, Germany plans to provide credit facilities for a period of six years, and the first payment will start from April next year.

Italy's Ambiguous Attitude: Japanese Ambassador Visits Italian Foreign Ministry 43

(Rome) Japanese Ambassador to Italy, Sugimura, recently visited Foreign Minister Ciano today to discuss matters. Responsible figures here do not want to make any announcements about whether Italy will participate in the anti-communist front between Japan and Germany. Political figures only said that Italy is very interested in the anti-communist agreement currently being negotiated between Germany and Japan and is closely watching the progress of the negotiations, because Italy's views on communism are the same as those of Germany and Japan. The article on the anti-communist agreement between Japan, Germany, and Italy published in the London Times this morning was only commented on by the "Tribune," which said, "We deeply regret this view of the Times and believe that the majority of British public opinion will condemn it." (According to the content of the Times article, see Reuter's telegram last night, (Havas telegram on the 18th)

(London) After the news of the conclusion of a military alliance between Germany and Japan came from Shanghai, rumors also arose in Europe. One rumor is that Italy may join this anti-communist alliance. Observers in Paris believe that Italy's attitude is quite cold. It is said that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini was quite disappointed with the recent Italian-German meeting, because German leader Hitler believed that Italy's Central European plan was not yet mature, so he could not agree to it. (National Electricity on the 18th)

American Commentator Arrives in Shanghai; Gives Speech; Does Not Believe Germany and Japan Will Form Alliance 44

The Continental Daily News reports that Mr. Chamberlain, a famous American commentator and Far East correspondent for the Christian Science Monitor, arrived in Shanghai on Wednesday aboard the Shanghai Maru steamer from Tokyo. Before leaving Tokyo, Mr. Chamberlain had a meeting with the spokesperson of the German Embassy. A few minutes after disembarking in Shanghai, Mr. Chamberlain told reporters, "I personally believe that Germany and Japan have not signed a military alliance. The two countries will not make this alliance, and will not guarantee each other's territory." Mr. Chamberlain also said that Germany is now eager to maintain friendly relations with China because Germany sees China as a large market for its goods. He touched on this point during his conversation with the spokesperson of the German Embassy in Japan. The spokesperson told him that Germany did not want to be involved in any disputes in this part of the world. According to Mr. Chamberlain, if Germany and Japan sign a military alliance, it will unite China and Russia. However, when the problem of Chinese communism has not been resolved, China will, of course, still be cautious with Soviet Russia. Mr. Chamberlain does not want to deny that the relationship between Germany and Japan has developed very satisfactorily recently. Commerce between Germany and Japan has developed greatly as a result. Mr. Chamberlain also does not want to deny that the friendly relations between the two countries may give rise to a declaration of common unity, which may be brewing between the two countries now, but it is not a military alliance. When someone asked Mr. Zhang whether his denial that Germany and Japan had signed a treaty was based on information obtained from white people, Mr. Zhang replied that the Japanese authorities were extremely silent on the matter. The spokesman of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs only said that this was just a revival of old rumors. Mr. Zhang's remarks are not based entirely on information obtained in Tokyo in recent days. Mr. Zhang is familiar with Far Eastern affairs, so he makes his conclusions based on his extensive experience. Mr. Zhang also felt that the possibility of a serious conflict between Russia and Japan has been greatly reduced in recent months due to the resolution of the northern fisheries and oil rights. Mr. Zhang is now scheduled to leave for the south next Monday to visit the Philippines, Singapore, and Siam. Mr. Zhang worked as a journalist in Russia for many years and is the author of "The Russian Revolution." He recently changed his position to Tokyo correspondent for the Christian Science Monitor.

British Industries Federation Establishes China Committee to Study China's Needs and Promote British Trade 45

(London) The British Industries Federation announced today the establishment of a special China Committee. The committee has a total of nine members, all of whom are experts in the Chinese market. The groups they represent include major engineering companies, the Federation of Diesel Engine Manufacturers, the Asiatic Petroleum Company, the British-American Tobacco Company, and Imperial Chemical Industries. The chairman is Sir McDonough, the current member of the London Committee of HSBC and the former president of the China Association. According to the secretary of the Federation, the reason for the establishment of the China Committee is partly due to Kirkpatrick's recent appointment as the representative of the Export Credit Guarantee Bureau in China. The Federation has seen that China's trade and finance have been greatly improved due to its currency reform and believes that the future is quite optimistic. However, the Federation believes that direct promotion by the government is necessary for greater effect. Therefore, it welcomes Mr. Kirkpatrick's appointment because he can provide valuable information on China's needs at any time. The task of the committee is to study China's needs and to enable British merchants to cooperate and provide various machines needed for a certain enterprise, such as a water plant. In addition to establishing a special China Committee, the Federation also gave various room equipment as a gift to the new house built by the Sino-British Cultural Association in Nanjing. Several other merchants also have gifts, including an electric clock and a radio. These gifts will be sent to China at the end of this month. (Reuter's telegram on the 19th)

America Will Continue to Purchase Silver from London in the Near Future 46

(Washington) Responsible sources here indicated today that the United States may need to purchase some silver from London in the near future. This will probably be implemented after the full amount of silver purchased from China under the agreement has been reached. At that time, purchasing silver from London will also avoid disrupting the market, so the bulk of the silver will still be purchased from silver-producing countries. (National Electricity on the 18th)

Zhu is related to Song Ziwen by marriage and uses Chinese emotions to write Western paintings. A total of fifty-one pieces were exhibited, mostly landscapes from Beijing to Scotland. Zhu will live in Morocco this winter to paint. (Reuter's telegram on the 18th)

Britain Reiterates Respect for the Nine-Power Treaty; Negotiating with Signatory Countries Regarding Japan's Actions in China 48

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden said in the House of Commons today in response to a question from a member of parliament that the British government will continue to uphold the Nine-Power Treaty to protect the integrity of China's territory. "The government is very concerned about the provisions of the treaty. Because the provisions of the treaty have been affected by Japan's Far East policy, we have been negotiating with other signatory countries, and we will continue this action in the future." American Good Neighbor Policy Replaces Outdated Monroe Doctrine; President Luo Travels to South America on the "Sea White House" 49

(New York) Two American "supreme salesmen" will be actively involved in major events in South America, one to sell the Good Neighbor Policy, and the other to seek the conclusion of reciprocal trade agreements. One of them is President Luo, who has already left Charleston on the 10,000-ton cruiser "Indianapolis" to attend the Pan-American Peace Conference that opens on December 1st in the capital of Argentina. The other is U.S. Secretary of State Hull, who is currently traveling from the capital of Brazil to Argentina. President Luo will widely sell his Good Neighbor Doctrine to replace the Monroe Doctrine, which is no longer applicable today. Hull will sell his reciprocal trade agreements. In addition to Argentina, President Luo will also visit the capitals of Brazil and Uruguay and will probably make small stops in other cities. The cruiser "Indianapolis" will be President Luo's "temporary White House" for the next month, and the cruiser "Chester" will accompany him. (Reuter's telegram on the 19th)

(New York) President Roosevelt, accompanied by his son James and several naval and army attendants, boarded a cruiser today to go to the capital of Argentina to personally convey a message of goodwill to the South American Peace Conference. When the cruiser set sail, the Fort Moltley battery fired a 21-gun salute to pay tribute. The President's ship also fired a gun salute in response. The President will communicate with the White House by radio along the way, and important mail will be delivered by plane every day. (National Army on the 18th)

Italian Fascist Party Decides to Accelerate Military Preparations and Seek Complete Economic Self-Sufficiency; Satisfied with Cooperation with Germany, Austria, and Hungary 50

(Rome) After meeting overnight, the Supreme Council of the Fascist Party announced today that it will accelerate military preparations as soon as possible. The communique stated, "After listening to Prime Minister Mussolini's detailed report on the country's military preparations, the council believes that in the current special period, these preparations must be accelerated, especially the navy and air force." The communique also declared that Italy is determined to reach the highest point of economic self-sufficiency and pay special attention to national defense. It also stated that the results of Foreign Minister Ciano's visits to the capitals of Austria and Hungary have laid the foundation for cooperation between Italy, Germany, Austria, and Hungary, which is gratifying. In addition, a committee was established to draft various proposals for organizing a new parliament of fascist professional groups. Generally, this move is regarded as a prelude to the abolition of the House of Representatives. General Balbo also rushed from Libya to attend. (Reuter's telegram on the 19th)

Countries Around the World Compete in Military Expansion; Military Expenditures Increase Sharply 51

(Geneva) According to the League of Nations' 1936 Armaments Yearbook statistics, countries around the world have spent more on military supplies such as munitions, warships, and aircraft than before. The total amount of world military expenditures in 1935 reached 5.4 billion yuan (calculated in 1933 US dollars, the same below), 4.9 billion yuan in 1934, and only 2.5 billion yuan in 1913. However, these statistics are not completely accurate because Germany keeps its military budget strictly secret. As for the world's navies, if the warships that have been built and those under construction are combined, they totaled 6.013 billion tons in 1935, and only 5.83 billion tons in 1934. The yearbook also stated that European countries are preparing for war in a hurry, and even train children to be soldiers. Italian children must receive compulsory military training from the age of eight until they enlist in the army. The period from eight to eighteen years old is the first period, and eighteen to twenty-one years old is the second period. After Austria violated the Treaty of Saint-Germain and established a conscription system, it also implemented military training in primary schools, middle schools, and agricultural schools. In Poland, all middle school students, high school students, and young people who do not attend school must receive military training. Within one year, 26,000 students and 133,000 non-students have undergone this training. Young people in Romania between the ages of eighteen and twenty-one must receive 50 days of military training every year. Other countries such as Sweden and Belgium also have voluntary training systems. (National Electricity on the 18th)

Vatican City Has a Population of 600 People and 176 Cars 52

According to official statistics, the Vatican City today has a total of 600 residents, but has 176 cars, including 145 passenger cars, 21 freight cars, and 10 motorcycles, making it the world's number one in terms of cars per person. (National Electricity on the 18th)

More Than a Thousand Casualties in the Spanish Capital; Bombing and Burning Have Not Stopped; Italy and Germany Recognize the Rebel Government; Britain and France Decide to Oppose the Rebel Blockade of Ports; Diplomatic Missions Meet for Humanitarian Appeal 53

(London) Some people here believe that the Spanish National Army plans to blockade the port of Barcelona to prevent Soviet arms from being imported there, followed by the recognition of the National Army government by Italy and Germany, which may lead to a new and significant situation. (Reuter's telegram on the 19th)

Madrid: The diplomatic corps recently met here, chaired by Chilean Ambassador Mogato. Diplomats from various countries believed that the Spanish civil war was so cruel that it made people feel that humanity was extinct and law and order was lost. For example, both sides indiscriminately bombed, causing innocent civilians to die in large numbers. We are on the scene and cannot remain silent. We should solemnly protest and express our deep hatred. (Havas telegram on the 19th)

Madrid: Several aircraft of the National Army repeated the bombing of the city at 2:45 this morning, first dropping rockets and then throwing many bombs, most of which fell near the 17-story building of the telephone bureau. The sound of explosions was deafening. (Havas telegram on the 19th)

Madrid: National Army aircraft bombed the capital at 2:30 and 9:00 this morning, causing hundreds of casualties. Five three-engine bombers participated in the second air raid, but only dropped four or five bombs and retreated due to resistance from government aircraft. (Reuter's telegram on the 19th)

Madrid: A Reuters special correspondent risked going out to inspect during a brief lull in the shelling and saw countless huge pits in the middle of the street, with broken walls and rubble everywhere. Some were still burning. Several large squares looked like scenes from war movies. He then went to visit friends on a certain street, but found that the whole family was dead. The situation has not changed today. The rebel side claims to have made progress in the northern district of the capital but has been heavily damaged by the fierce artillery fire of the defending army. According to the government's radio station, more than 40,000 fresh troops are coming to the capital to help in the war. The famous bullfighter Beipu, who is now an officer in the National Army, said while watching the night battle on the tower of General Farila's headquarters the other day, "We are just like Emperor Nero watching the Great Fire of Rome." This statement is very accurate because flames are soaring everywhere in the city of Madrid, and planes are dropping hundreds of fire umbrellas, descending slowly to facilitate bombers to choose their targets. (Reuter's telegram on the 18th)

Madrid: According to semi-official sources, yesterday's bombing of Madrid killed 250 people and injured 800 people. In the past week, the death toll has reached 500 and the injury toll has reached 1,200, mostly women and children. The once bustling streets are now ashes, and the magnificent palace has also been mostly destroyed. Buildings around the famous Puerta del Sol Square in the center of Madrid are still burning. The tram tracks have also been destroyed, and the underground station is full of rubble. The Free Newspaper building is now ablaze. National Army aircraft have dropped leaflets from the sky, threatening that if the defending army does not surrender, the army's aircraft will intensify night attacks.

Madrid: The rebels bombed Madrid yesterday, killing more than 300 people and injuring 800 people, and it has not stopped today. Last night, a bomb fell on the South Station, killing many people. Passengers fled into the ground, and several people were buried alive by bombs in the cellar of Maitala Street, while others suffocated to death. (National Electricity on the 18th)

Germany and Italy Issue Similar Announcements 54

(Berlin) Today, both Italy and Germany recognized the revolutionary government organized by General Franco as the official government of Spain. The German official announcement stated: "The government organized by General Franco controls the largest territory. Recent developments indicate that it will soon exercise power in other areas. The German government, in view of these facts, has decided to recognize it and has dispatched a chargé d'affaires to establish diplomatic relations. The new German chargé d'affaires will present his credentials to General Franco. The current German chargé d'affaires in Alicante will be recalled." It is reported that Rome has also issued a similar announcement. In addition, German propaganda officials confirmed that this joint action by Germany and Italy was anticipated due to the imminent fall of Madrid. However, they declined to comment on whether the purpose of this action was to prevent Soviet aid to the Spanish government forces. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Berlin) According to official sources, General Franco, commander-in-chief of the Spanish Nationalist forces, is now able to control a large part of Spanish territory. Germany's recognition is a natural step. However, as a member of the Non-Intervention Adjustment Committee, Germany's position as a signatory to the Non-Intervention Agreement will not be changed as a result. (Reuters, 19th)

(Berlin) Foreign Ministry officials recently stated that Germany's recognition of the Spanish Nationalist government was announced simultaneously with Italy because, during Italian Foreign Minister Ciano's recent visit to Germany, the two countries agreed to adopt a common policy against Bolshevism. The joint recognition of the Burgos government is based on this fact. (Havas, 18th)

(London) Both Germany and Italy have recognized the government organized by General Franco, commander-in-chief of the Spanish Nationalist forces. Once the Nationalist forces completely control Madrid, the government will move from Burgos to the capital. British observers were greatly surprised by this move, although they anticipated it eventually. They believed it would have been at the earliest only after the Nationalist forces occupied the entire city of Madrid. This place views the steps taken by the German and Italian governments as merely a formal expression of sympathy for General Franco, a sympathy that both countries have not concealed. Responsible circles in Britain believe that both Germany and Italy have made promises not to intervene in the Spanish Civil War and should abide by them. Therefore, the decisions of the two governments will not change the status of the Non-Intervention Agreement. As for the British government, it has no intention of abandoning its non-intervention policy. It is expected that in the near future, someone will ask the British government to state its attitude towards the Franco government. (Reuters, 19th)

(London) The British government must continue to adhere to the Non-Intervention Agreement. Britain will vigorously oppose any attempt to release the obligations borne by the signatory countries of the Non-Intervention Agreement. As for the date of the next meeting of the Adjustment Committee, it is currently not determined. (Havas, 18th)

(Paris) French authorities expected that Italy and Germany would recognize the Spanish Nationalist government, but they did not expect the recognition to happen so quickly. According to political circles, the result of this move may be that the two countries will openly supply military equipment to the Spanish Nationalist forces and believe that their motive is partly to enable the Nationalist forces to search ships suspected of carrying military supplies without violating international law. However, France will not allow the Nationalist forces to have the right to search such ships because of this move by Germany and Italy and will take necessary measures in the Mediterranean to protect French ships and declare that France's policy on non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War has not changed in any way. (Reuters, 19th)

(Vienna) Well-informed sources predict that the governments of Austria and Hungary will soon recognize the Spanish Nationalist government. During the recent meeting of the foreign ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary in Vienna, it was decided that after Italy recognizes the Nationalist government, Austria and Hungary should follow suit. Currently, the Austrian envoy to Spain has not yet presented his credentials to the Spanish Popular Front government, so it is very easy for Austria to withdraw its diplomatic representatives from Madrid. (Havas, 18th)

According to news from Paris, the French naval minister and foreign minister will take appropriate measures to ensure the safety of French citizens and French merchant ships. (Reuters, 19th)

Spanish Court Sentences Former Dictator's Son to Death 55

Alicante - José Antonio Primo de Rivera, son of the deceased dictator General Rivera, and leader of the Falangist party, was arrested for rebellion and inciting military mutiny. His brother Miguel and sister-in-law Margarita were also arrested one after another. All were tried by the People's Front Court here. José Antonio has been sentenced to death. Miguel has been sentenced to 30 years in prison. Margarita has been sentenced to six years of detention. José Antonio requested a reduction of the sentence to life imprisonment, but it was rejected by the court. (Havas, 18th)

Rebel Army Announces Blockade of Seaports, Britain and France Negotiate Naval Cooperation 56

British Air Force: Domestic Strength Increases to Eighty Squadrons, First-Line Strength Reaches Nine Hundred Aircraft 59

(London) According to the most recently published survey, the strength of the British Royal Air Force stationed in various domestic squadrons has greatly increased since May of last year. In May 1935, there were a total of fifty-three squadrons stationed in the country, possessing 580 first-line aircraft. Currently, the number of squadrons stationed in the country has increased to eighty, and the number of first-line aircraft has also expanded to 992. From the above figures, it can be seen that the progress of the British Air Force is rapid. The goal of one hundred and twenty-nine squadrons and one thousand seven hundred and fifty first-line aircraft is not difficult to achieve in a short period of time. The British Air Ministry plans to build fifty new aircraft fields, and thirty-nine are currently under construction. The locations of the various aircraft fields are mostly in the south and southeast of England. It is reported that the current balloon barrier has a considerable effect on the consolidation of London's air defense and has proven to be even more effective in cloudy weather, as it can make it difficult for fighter planes to track bombers. (Reuters, 19th)

Austrian Foreign Minister Arrives in Berlin for Important Negotiations and Conclusion of Economic Agreement 62

(Vienna) Foreign Minister Dr. Schmidt is now in Berlin to conclude an economic agreement with Germany to enable Austria to engage in large-scale rearmament. Dr. Schmidt's visit to Germany is the first official visit by an Austrian cabinet member to Germany in four years. It is generally believed that Dr. Schmidt's trip, accompanied by the German ambassador to Austria, von Papen, is particularly noteworthy. The proposed plan stipulates that Germany purchase Austria's surplus milk and timber, while Germany sells military aircraft, tanks, and heavy artillery to Austria. So far, negotiations between the two countries have stalled due to Germany's excessively low prices for Austrian goods, such as offering only two pence per pound of butter. However, it is widely believed that Dr. Schmidt's mission to Germany is to try to remove obstacles to Austria's rearmament, as Austria is determined to do so. This is evidenced by the conscription that began in April of this year, the 6% increase in military spending, and the declaration of the right to rearm on November 12. (Reuters, 18th)

Former French Interior Minister Dies of Slander, Heartrending Suicide Note, Vigorously Clears Himself of Treason, His Suicide Should Be the Responsibility of Those Who Slandered Him 63

Lille - Former French Minister of Interior, Salengro, who committed suicide yesterday after newspapers and the Chamber of Deputies claimed that he had acted cowardly during the European War, has now had a suicide note discovered which was addressed to the French Prime Minister Blum. The wording within the note is extremely tragic and moving. One passage reads, "My wife died because I was slandered. My mother also became mentally ill because of it. Although I struggled hard, I ultimately failed. I myself have now been poisoned. They cannot tarnish my character, but they should be held responsible for my suicide. I have never committed treason. The party to which I belong is my life." When Blum read this letter, tears welled up in his eyes. He lowered his head and stood silently before Salengro's remains for several minutes. It is reported that Salengro committed suicide at home yesterday by turning on the gas. (Reuters, 19th)

Yan Xishan Destroys His Home to Relieve the National Crisis: Following His Mother's Instructions, He Donates His Late Father's Estate of 870,000 Yuan to the Finance Department to Be Used for Military Expenses in Suiyuan Province 68

Taiyuan Correspondence: Yan Xishan, Director of the Taiyuan Pacification Headquarters, recently received instructions from his mother that, in view of the current grave national crisis and the heavy burden on the people, and with various places donating funds to reward the soldiers and boost morale, he should donate his late father, Ziming's, entire estate, totaling 870,000 yuan, for national salvation purposes, setting an example for the world by destroying his home to relieve the national crisis. After receiving the order, Yan immediately convened a family meeting and allocated the funds as requested, handing them over to the Shanxi Provincial Department of Finance for receipt and distribution. He also sent a letter to the Finance Department, instructing them to dispatch personnel immediately to take stock of the funds. The letter stated, "Respectfully, I received a kind instruction from my mother yesterday, saying, 'The national crisis is so severe, and people across the country are donating funds to aid Suiyuan. You, as the senior official of Jin and Sui, should especially take the lead. Moreover, destroying your home to relieve the national crisis was your father's dying wish. You should immediately donate your father's estate of 870,000 yuan for national salvation purposes. I believe you will also be happy to do so.' I should naturally comply with the order and have the funds allocated by the administrators for receipt by your department. To the Department of Finance, Yan Xishan, November 11th."

Regarding the matter, Zhao Daiwen, Chairman of the Provincial Government, made a detailed report during the memorial week held at the Sui Office and the Provincial Government on the morning of the 16th, stating, "On the 11th of this month, Director Yan sent a letter to the Department of Finance (original text above). When Mr. Yan's late father, Ziming, was ill, he designated a portion of his family property to be donated: 50,000 yuan to Shanxi Province, 30,000 yuan to Wutai County, and 20,000 yuan to Hebian Village, to be used as social welfare funds. Director Yan has already carried out these instructions. I also recall that when the old gentleman was on his deathbed, I accompanied Director Yan at his side and personally heard him say to Director Yan, 'I have engaged in some business throughout my life and have accumulated some savings. If the country faces difficulties in the future, you can donate all of it to the country for national salvation purposes,' and instructed the old lady to take care of the matter. Now, the old lady, in view of the severity of the national crisis, has instructed Director Yan to carry out the old gentleman's will. My feelings about this matter are very deep. The Book of Rites says, 'It is good to accumulate wealth and be able to distribute it,' but it is far less significant than 'destroying your home to relieve the national crisis.' Everyone, think about it, what use of wealth could be greater or more meaningful than using it to save the country? There is definitely none. We should all think deeply about this."

North China Air Service Begins: Opening Ceremony Held in Tianjin on the 17th; Nine Aircraft Assigned to Four Routes 69

Tianjin Correspondence: Preparations for the Sino-Japanese air service have been underway for nearly two months. Today, the opening ceremony of the Huitong General Aviation Company was held on the 17th, and air service will officially begin on the 18th. The opening ceremony was held at the newly built airfield in front of the Japanese barracks in Li Mingzhuang in the eastern suburbs of Tianjin. The airfield has a newly built hangar that can accommodate ten aircraft. Around 9 a.m. that day, Chinese and foreign dignitaries arrived one after another. For a time, the Dongjuzi Road was bustling with traffic. At 10 a.m. sharp, dozens of people arrived, including Tianjin Mayor Zhang Zizhong, Tianjin Security Commander Liu Jialuan, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau Chen Juesheng, Song Zheyuan's representative Zhang Bi, Qin Dechun's representatives Liu Shifu and Wang Yitang, Cao Rulin, and Lu Zongyu. From the Japanese side came Commander Tadashi, Consul General Horiuchi, Chief of Staff Hashimoto, Naval Attaché to Tianjin Kubota, and military staff including Iide, Kazu, and Ikeda, and Sentada, totaling dozens of people. Together with guests from all walks of life, there were over 300 attendees. During the ceremony, the band played the Chinese and Japanese national anthems. Chairman Zhang Yunrong and Vice Chairman Kodama Tsuneo of Huitong Aviation Company then gave speeches in Chinese and Japanese, respectively, reporting on the preparations. They stated, "Today, our company is holding its opening ceremony. We are honored and grateful for the presence of all the guests and the congratulatory letters and telegrams from friends from all sides. I can report to everyone in detail on the preparations of our company. The issue of Sino-Japanese air service has been discussed for a long time. It was proposed during the Beiping Political Affairs Committee of the Executive Yuan. When Wang Kemin was the chairman, it was discussed several times, but it was ultimately deemed too hasty, and no decision was made. This time, the Japanese side brought up the old matter again, and Chairman Song continued the previous proposal of the central government and negotiated again. Fortunately, both sides were able to conduct sincere discussions based on the spirit of equality and mutual benefit and reached a general decision in the shortest possible time, entrusting Yunrong and others to step up preparations and plan in detail. Now, the preparations are complete, and we have decided to hold the opening ceremony today. The company's capital was originally set at 4.5 million, to be borne equally by both sides. The flight routes will be centered on Tianjin, initially opening four routes: Tianjin to Dalian, Tianjin to Jinzhou, Tianjin to Chengde, and Tianjin to Zhangjiakou. The aircraft equipment is designed for comfort, and the ticket prices are designed to be affordable. In terms of technology, we have experienced pilots from both China and Japan. We also plan to establish night flights to seek new developments in the history of transportation. As for the company's organization, it fully complies with the Chinese Company Law, first submitting to the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee through the local government for record-keeping, and then requesting the competent department from the Political Affairs Committee for registration. In terms of management, we have decided to adopt a board system, with the board of directors fully handling all matters and taking responsibility for sound development. Both sides are determined to maintain this spirit of equality and mutual benefit from beginning to end, seeking co-existence and co-prosperity. Since the establishment of our company, transportation has become more convenient, and there will inevitably be great contributions and developments in East Asian culture, commerce, and economy. However, at the beginning of the establishment, there are bound to be some crude and simple aspects. We hope that all parties will provide guidance and supervision at any time so that this great undertaking can advance with each passing day. Our company will definitely accept it sincerely to meet the expectations of everyone." Subsequently, Zhang Bi gave a congratulatory speech on behalf of Song Zheyuan, and Tadashi gave a speech. Zhang Zizhong and Horiuchi also gave congratulatory speeches. Then, Liu Shifu, representing Qin Dechun, read congratulatory telegrams. Feng Zhian, Liu Ruming, Japanese Foreign Minister Arita, Army Minister Terauchi, Minister of Communications Raimu, Navy Minister Nagano, and the Kwantung Army also sent congratulatory messages, which were read one by one. The ceremony ended around 11 a.m. A picnic was then held inside the hangar. Tadashi raised his glass and shouted "Long live Huitong" three times. At that time, eight aircraft formed a formation in the sky, performing technical maneuvers. Then, the company presented each guest with two Japanese-style pastries, a wine glass, and two cards. From 11:30 a.m., guests were invited in batches to take a flight around the city for sightseeing for a week, which lasted until 1 p.m.

The company was originally scheduled to start air service on the 17th, but it was postponed by one day due to preparations and implemented on the 18th. The four routes were opened on the same day. There are a total of nine aircraft: one large Ford eight-seater aircraft, registration number 502; six Ford medium-sized aircraft, each with six seats, registration numbers "127," "128," "140," "1101," "1102," and "504"; and two Pasi small aircraft, each with two seats, registration numbers "1103" and "1104." These nine aircraft will temporarily maintain transportation. The large aircraft will operate on the Tianjin-Dalian route, the medium-sized aircraft will operate on the Beijing-Tianjin, Tianjin-Jinzhou, and Tianjin-Beijing routes, and the small aircraft will operate on the Tianjin-Chengde route. The Tianjin-Dalian route has frequent traffic, and it is planned to add two Douglas aircraft in the future, which can be realized next month. According to Zhang Yunrong, the company will start business tomorrow and is divided into four groups: the General Affairs Group, under which there are General Affairs and Planning Sections; the Business Group, under which there are Business, Accounting, and Supply Sections; the Aviation Group, which has Navigation and Communications Sections; and the Education Group, which has Education and Maintenance Sections. There are a total of seven directors, four from our side and three from the Japanese side. There are 60 employees, half Chinese and half Japanese. However, feeling the lack of pilot talent, it was decided to set up an aviation training class to cultivate talent. From now on, this company will be responsible for air transportation, and Japanese aircraft will no longer fly to Tianjin. The Tianjin-Baotou route was proposed by the Japanese side, but it is difficult to realize it for the time being. The matter of attaching mail can also be discussed later, but it will not be held for the moment. At 7 p.m. on the 17th, the Chinese and Japanese chairmen of Huitong Aviation Company specially hosted a reception at the Japanese Residents Association in the Japanese Concession to celebrate the company's establishment, attended by over 140 people including Zhang Zizhong, Tadashi, Wang Yitang, Cao Rulin, Chen Zhongfu, Hashimoto, and Horiuchi. The aviation negotiations concluded amid cheers. (17th)

Feng's inauguration date in Baoding will be after Song returns from southern Hebei, around the 20th. At that time, Song will introduce Feng to the heads of the various departments and commissions. As for the 37th Division commanded by Feng, it will be moved to Baoding for garrison duty. From then on, Feng will be stationed here for a long time so that he can attend to military and political affairs at any time. After Feng's inauguration, Song will return to Beiping immediately. Song's special train has already departed from Beiping and arrived in Baoding, ready for use. It may travel from Baoding south to Handan for Song to use when he returns north from southern Hebei. Nanhui: Zhuhqiao Township Flower Factory Robbed 72

The Dingxiangfeng Flower Factory in Zhuhqiao Township, Second District, was suddenly attacked by eight bandits with a Hakka accent at around 2 a.m. the day before yesterday. At the same time, they are finding ways to raise funds separately to console the soldiers defending the country. Suzhou Mingbao, Wuxian Daily, and Suzhou Early News are collecting donations on behalf of the public. Once a certain amount is collected, they will be remitted to Suiyuan to support the army. All police personnel in the county are working to conserve food and raise funds. Various schools will hold large-scale fundraising and support movements for Suiyuan in the coming days. The Wuxian County Party Headquarters will convene representatives from various agencies, groups, and schools at Zhongshan Hall at 3 p.m. on the 19th to discuss expanding support for Suiyuan. The chairman is Sun Danchen. It was decided to establish a support association for soldiers defending the country in Suiyuan, appoint personnel to actively carry out support efforts, and strengthen national defense.

Wuxi: All Circles Console the Soldiers in Suiyuan 74

The border violations by the puppet bandits and the outbreak of the war in Suiyuan are of great importance to the nation and the people. Our soldiers at the front are defending the territory of the country in the freezing cold and fighting the bandits and puppets. All countrymen should fulfill their national duties and provide spiritual or material comfort to the soldiers who are defending the territory and loyal to the country. Various agencies and groups in this county, such as the County Party Headquarters, the County Government, and the County Chamber of Commerce, as well as the silk factory labor union and various schools, have been stirred by patriotic zeal and are enthusiastically contributing to provide powerful assistance. At the same time, all personnel of the local court donated 136.30 yuan and remitted it to the front to provide condolences. In addition, all 149 detainees in the court's detention center voluntarily fasted for one day yesterday (the 19th), and the money saved was sent to the front line, which is especially inspiring. In addition, Xing Yuantang, the warden of the Jiangsu Fifth Prison, and all staff members, used one day's income to console the soldiers resisting the enemy.

Changshu: Large Centipede Found on Dingshan Mountain 75

The Dingshan area outside the North Gate of this city is mostly mountainous. In addition to farming, residents rely on the mountain's products as their biggest sideline. In autumn and winter, residents must climb the mountains to prune trees and cut firewood. On the afternoon of the 18th, Xu Gengsong was cutting firewood when he suddenly discovered a large centipede in a valley. It was over two feet long, as thick as a flat buckle, and had a red glow on its head. It moved very quickly. Upon seeing it, Xu was extremely frightened and ran to tell his neighbors. According to the crowd, such a giant creature must have a pearl on its body. The crowd immediately climbed the mountain with weapons to search and capture it. After three hours, they found nothing. For a time, it was rumored as a strange tale.

Nantong: Consoling the Soldiers on the Suiyuan Border 76

Representatives from various agencies, groups, and commercial and agricultural circles in Nantong held a joint meeting at 2 p.m. on the 18th. It was decided to organize a joint association of all circles in Nantong to console the soldiers at the front. Ge Tan and ten others were appointed as members to raise funds to console the Suiyuan border.

Yangzhou: Large Number of Bandits Captured 77

Recently, banditry has been rampant in the third district of this county, with robberies occurring frequently. The Jiangdu Public Security Detective Team received a report that a large number of bandit ships were docked in the area. The deputy captain of the detective team, Zhang Qingan, led the detectives to disguise themselves and investigate. They first encountered several bandit ships at the mouth of the Sanjiangying River and interrogated them. The police and bandits exchanged fire, and the bandits were unable to resist. As a result, six bandits were captured. Later, it was learned from the bandits that the remaining members were hiding in Dadaokou in Yangzhong County. The team rushed to Changzai Yangjia County, Shuangjiangkou, and encountered the bandits. They exchanged fire for the second time, resulting in the capture of five more bandits. A total of eleven bandits were captured, along with five bandit ship guns. They were escorted back to Yangzhou at 8 p.m. on the 18th, and the team interrogated them strictly.

Haizhou: Tongpu-Longhai Through Transport 78

In order to develop the Longhai Railway's business and promote Lianyungang, the Longhai Railway Authority is now in negotiation with Tongpu Railway Authority to establish through transport. In the future, goods from Tongpu Railway will be transferred to Longhai Railway and then exported from Lianyungang. Recently, goods have piled up in Lianyungang like mountains, which is a great improvement compared to the previous month. However, due to the lack of railway cars and the delay in ship transportation, the transfer of goods has been slightly slower.

Hangzhou: Liu Zhen Travels to Moganshan 79

Liu Zhenbao recently traveled to Moganshan with friends via Hangzhou and then went to Tianmushan and other places for sightseeing. He will return to Shanghai in a week.

Shaoxing: National Labor Service Methods 80

Shaoxing National Labor Service: The county government has ordered that construction begin. The district offices in the urban area have scheduled a meeting of the five township heads on the 25th to discuss the methods. The main tasks of this project are to renovate Tashan Mountain and dredge river channels. The date is tentatively set for three days. If a strong man is unable to report to work due to unforeseen circumstances, he must pay a substitute service fee of 30 cents per day.

Taizhou: Rafts Encountered Bandits and Were Burned 81

Xie Fei Timber Firm, located in the Shuijiang area bordering Wenling and Yueqing, recently purchased thirteen rafts of timber from Qingtian, totaling one unit. While sailing through the Panshiyang waters off Wenzhou, they were suddenly attacked by over twenty pirates led by Yan Yikun. They demanded a protection fee, and when this was unsuccessful, they set fire to all the timber with kerosene, resulting in a loss of over 3,000 yuan.
