Chairman Fu's Victory Telegram Arrives in Shanghai: Many Bandits Killed, Countless Weapons Captured 82

A certain military authority in this city has received two consecutive telegrams from Chairman Fu in Suiyuan, reporting on the battle situation against the bandits in the past few days and the situation of the bandit army being pushed back yesterday. The telegrams are summarized as follows:

Telegram from Qia (title omitted): On the morning of the 15th, the puppet troops began to attack Honggeqiangtu, which belongs to Taolin. Prior to this, seven aircraft were used for reconnaissance and bombing. There were fierce battles in the morning and evening, which were all resolutely repelled by our cavalry guard regiment. Many bandits were killed. The bandits repeatedly attacked without success. In the afternoon, seven more aircraft came for fierce bombing and machine-gun strafing. I, Fu Zuoyi, report to you.

Telegram from Qiao (title omitted): In recent days, the bandits have repeatedly launched fierce attacks on Honggeqiangtu, under the cover of aircraft artillery and machine guns, and using ladders, but have not succeeded. Yesterday, we dispatched additional infantry and artillery units, arriving overnight. The banditry was attacked by surprise there at 2 a.m. this morning, rushing towards the bandit nests in Dala Village, Tuchengzi and other places belonging to Shangdu. After more than three hours of fierce fighting, the bandits collapsed, killing many bandits and capturing many automobiles, radio stations, and supplies. Our army also suffered casualties from the fierce bombing by the bandit aircraft. In addition, the bandit troops of Li Shouxin and Zhang Wanqing, numbering four to five thousand, moved toward that side from Nanhachien yesterday. In the afternoon, more than a thousand bandits were discovered in Fengmin Township and other villages northeast of the county. After resistance by the local security team, the bandits were held in check, and 1,500 bandits were repelled by our security team of over eighty people, capturing eleven people. I, Fu Zuoyi, report to you.

Italian Embassy Adds a Commercial Counselor 91

The first counselor, Mr. An Qilong, arrives in Shanghai. Dr. An Qilong, the newly appointed Commercial Counselor of the Italian Embassy in China, has arrived in Shanghai on the Italian Trieste Company's motor ship Victoria. Dr. An will organize and guide the new commercial delegation in Shanghai to consolidate and develop commercial relations between China and Italy. Dr. An is a graduate of the University of Rome and served as the Commercial Counselor of the Italian Embassy in the United States for twelve years. He served as an army captain in the European War and later went to Washington and London on government missions of an economic and financial nature. He is scheduled to establish the office of the Commercial Counselor of the Italian Embassy at No. 26 The Bund in early December.

Mellor Confers with Kung: The Anti-Smuggling Office Will Not Be Moved Elsewhere: Nearly in a State of Suspension: Smugglers are Very Active: More Than 40 Million in Tax Evasion on the Beining Railway This Year 92

Shenshi News Agency reported that the Road Transport Anti-Smuggling Inspection Office, after being moved from Beijing to Tianjin, has been unable to carry out its work actively due to various reasons. Recently, due to conflicts with customs anti-smuggling, there has been talk of moving it elsewhere, resulting in a state of suspension. Deputy Director Li Tonghua specially came to Shanghai a few days ago to visit Inspector General of Customs Mellor to ask for instructions. He has already gone to Beijing. Mellor reported the situation to Finance Minister Kung and was summoned to meet with Kung to discuss solutions. It was decided not to move the Road Transport Anti-Smuggling Inspection Office and to order Ansell to go north immediately to carry out anti-smuggling work. The Shenshi News Agency reporter learned from relevant sources yesterday that during the period when the road anti-smuggling inspection work was suspended, the Jidong area took the opportunity to carry out large-scale smuggling. Various unscrupulous merchants also took advantage of this to purchase and stockpile in large quantities. A certain merchant bank specially provided loans to support smugglers, with a huge amount. According to estimates from certain sources, from January to the end of October this year, the smuggled goods transported to Tianjin via the Beining Railway resulted in more than 40 million in tax evasion, mainly artificial silk and cotton cloth. Furthermore, according to the reporter's investigation, the smuggled goods stockpiled by unscrupulous merchants in North China, such as artificial silk and cotton cloth, have recently colluded with Japanese ruffians to transport them south, selling them in various places by breaking them into smaller lots. A certain yarn factory in this port even sent an employee to Tianjin to contact them. If smuggled goods were transported to Shanghai, they would be temporarily stored in the factory and then contact unscrupulous merchants to change their appearance and find ways to sell them. Most of them were also artificial silk. Recently, the factory has plans to set up an artificial silk factory to cover up the situation.

Red Cross General Headquarters: Suiyuan Committee Established: A Total of 43 Committee Members: Fundraising to Begin on the First of Next Month 97

The General Headquarters of the Chinese Red Cross Society, in light of the emergency in Suiyuan and the urgent need to step up work, has specially established an Economic Committee and held its first meeting. The members of the Economic Committee of the society are all local celebrities, and their names are as follows: Wang Rutang (Chairman), Du Yue (Vice Chairman), Liu Hongsheng (Vice Chairman), Lin Kanghou, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Qian Xinzhi, Yu Zuoting, Mu Ouchu, Song Hanzhang, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Weiru (Standing Committee Members), Wu Tiecheng, Zhu Ziqiao, Ye Yuhu, Yao Mulian, Zhao Jinqing, Xu Xinliu, Zhu Yinjiang, Zai Boqi, Jin Tingxun, Tang Shoumin, Chen Guangfu, Qin [censored], Ye Fuxiao, Lu Xuepu, Gu Xinyi, Ye Zuotang, Wen Lanting, Wang Yiting, Guan Jiongzhi, Lu Bohong, Huang Hanzhi, Yao Yuqin, Shen Lianfang, Lao Jingxiu, Di Chuqing, Zhu Meixian, Sun Hengfu, Wu Yunzhai, Wang Boyuan, Jin Jianxiang, and Wang Peiyuan (Committee Members). The society was established yesterday and immediately convened its first meeting. Chairman Wang Rutang presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals. Then, two proposals were discussed: (1) The organizational regulations of this committee have been drafted and proposed for discussion. Resolution: Amended and passed. (2) In this extraordinary period, raising funds for rescue is urgent. According to the reports of Director General Yan and Deputy Director Pang of the Rescue Committee, the need for funds is enormous (estimated at 570,000 yuan for the whole year, and approximately 150,000 yuan for the present). How should we raise the funds? Resolution: Each member of this committee will be responsible for raising 5,000 yuan, and fundraising brochures will be printed. Fundraising will be conducted from December 1st of this year to January 31st, 1937, and completed within these two months. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Jianghai Customs Announces October Figures: Shanghai's Import Surplus Exceeds 10 Million, Imports at 32,682,397 Yuan, Exports at 31,280,463 Yuan 98

According to the announcement yesterday by Jianghai Customs, Shanghai's foreign trade for October this year showed an increase in both import and export volumes compared to the same period last year, with a sharp increase in the import surplus. Imports were mainly composed of metals, minerals, and machinery, while exports mainly consisted of textiles, fibers, animals, and their products. A reporter from the Sin Chew News Agency has compiled the following detailed report:

October Import and Export Overview

In October this year, Shanghai's foreign trade recorded imports of 42,682,397 yuan and exports of 31,280,463 yuan, resulting in an import surplus of 11,401,934 yuan. Compared to September's imports of 48,292,851 yuan and exports of 32,925,545 yuan, both figures showed a slight decrease. However, compared to the same period last year, imports were 29,917,896 yuan, showing a sharp increase of 12,764,501 yuan. Exports were 28,342,416 yuan, showing an increase of 2,928,047 yuan. The import surplus of 9,826,454 yuan during the same period last year also increased sharply by 1,575,480 yuan.

Main Categories of Imported Goods

The main categories of imported goods in October included: various cotton cloths at 2,663,758 yuan; other cotton products at 63,715 yuan; hemp and its products at 721,370 yuan; wool and its products at 2,511,138 yuan; rayon and other products at 825,570 yuan; metals and minerals at 5,942,262 yuan; machinery and its tools at 2,100,132 yuan; vehicles and ships at 1,321,423 yuan; miscellaneous metal products at 2,829,180 yuan; fish, shellfish, and seafood at 868,208 yuan; canned food at 505,697 yuan; coarse grains and flour at 232,161 yuan; fruits, seeds, and vegetables at 439,451 yuan; medicinal materials and spices at 109,508 yuan; sugar at 457,052 yuan; wines and other beverages at 86,397 yuan; tobacco at 747,572 yuan; chemical products at 1,961,878 yuan; dyes and pigments at 2,624,250 yuan; candles, petroleum, oil, glue, and rosin at 3,999,505 yuan; books, maps, and wooden paper at 3,911,944 yuan; raw hides and other animal products at 172,834 yuan; timber at 860,260 yuan; wood, bamboo, rattan, palm, and their products at 349,098 yuan; fuel coal at 201,310 yuan; porcelain, glass, etc. at 205,883 yuan; stone, earth, and their products at 129,800 yuan; general merchandise at 5,645,191 yuan, totaling 42,682,379 yuan.

Main Categories of Exported Goods

The main categories of exported goods in October included: goods and their products at 3,848,010 yuan; leather, etc. at 582,600 yuan; fish, shellfish, and seafood at 24,354 yuan; beans at 660,983 yuan; miscellaneous grains and their products at 3,005,587 yuan; vegetable dyes at 57,276 yuan; fresh fruit, dried fruit, and processed fruit at 38,446 yuan; medicinal materials and spices at 38,675 yuan; oil at 2,304,113 yuan; seeds at 1,670,069 yuan; wine at 15,480 yuan; tea at 2,098,506 yuan; tobacco at 268,465 yuan; vegetables at 146,419 yuan; other plant products at 237,224 yuan; bamboo at 34,317 yuan; fuel at 23,092 yuan; rattan at 7,297 yuan; timber and its products at 85,754 yuan; paper at 87,900 yuan; textiles and fibers at 6,191,552 yuan; yarn, thread, and knitted goods at 3,514,732 yuan; cotton cloth at 1,531,912 yuan; other textiles at 1,954 yuan; ore and metal products at 2,278,580 yuan; glass and glass products at 14,981 yuan; stone, clay, sand, and their products at 189,966 yuan; chemicals at 299,719 yuan; printed materials at 200,433 yuan; general merchandise at 1,151,637 yuan, totaling 31,280,463 yuan.

Gold and Silver Import and Export Statistics

Furthermore, the import and export status of gold and silver in this port in October was as follows: imports were 86,676 customs taels of gold and 86,000 silver dollars, while exports were 7,051,376 customs taels of gold and 30,000,000 silver dollars. Cumulatively, from January onwards, gold imports totaled 1,040,054 customs taels, of which 441 customs taels were imported from India, 761,137 customs taels from the United Kingdom, 269,300 customs taels from Hong Kong, and 5,190 customs taels from Japan. Gold exports were only to the United Kingdom, totaling 16,239,122 customs taels. Silver imports totaled 1,717,178 yuan, of which 1,711,000 yuan were from Hong Kong and 4,489 yuan from Japan. Silver exports totaled 253,548,732 yuan, of which 661,961 yuan were to the United Kingdom, 36,000,000 yuan to Hong Kong, 100 yuan to Japan, and 216,886,471 yuan to the United States.

The Chinese Commissioner for the Yunnan-Burma Border Demarcation, Liang Yu-gao, is Scheduled to Fly to Yunnan Today; Issues Important Statement Before Departure 99

Mr. Liang Yu-gao, the chief commissioner of the Chinese-British Joint Yunnan-Burma Southern Section Boundary Affairs Committee, made the following statement to the National News Agency reporter:

"Regarding the Yunnan-Burma border demarcation work, I have been assigned to continue the demarcation of the Yunnan-Burma boundary. I am scheduled to fly to Yunnan from Shanghai on the 20th of this month, leading all the staff directly to the border area. Before departure, I have a few words to say to the people of the country. Our country has a vast territory and is bordered by many powerful nations, so boundary disputes have been constant from the Qing Dynasty to the present day. Among those in the southwest, the most important is the undemarcated Yunnan-Burma border. The undemarcated border is divided into northern and southern sections. The northern section concerns Pianma, Jiangxinpo, and other places, while the southern section includes Lufang, Ban Hong, Ximeng, and other areas. These areas are extremely rich in mineral resources, especially gold and silver. The dispute lies in these resources. Last year, I was appointed as the chief commissioner of the Chinese side of the Chinese-British Joint Yunnan-Burma Southern Section Boundary Affairs Committee. I entered the mountains in winter, met with the British commissioners and the neutral chairman appointed by the League of Nations, and conducted on-site surveys, enduring hardship and exposure to the elements. By April of this spring, due to the approaching rainy season, the meeting was adjourned and we returned to Beijing. However, in terms of work, only half of the overall task was completed. Therefore, this session will continue the work to achieve full success. The Sino-British joint survey of the southern section of the Yunnan-Burma border is based on the exchange of notes between the two governments on April 9, 1935. This document has already been published, and I believe readers have already read it. The Boundary Affairs Committee is composed of five commissioners, with China and Britain each having two, and a neutral commissioner selected by the League of Nations as chairman to impartially adjudicate all disputes. The work of the committee is to interpret Articles 2, 3, and 4 of the 1897 treaty (Guangxu 23rd year), i.e., to determine the true meaning of the treaty based on on-site surveys of geographical, political, and historical factors. The details of this are all in the Terms of Reference of the committee, which I will not repeat here. However, there are two points that I hope the people of the country will pay attention to: (1) The survey work is based on the old treaty and provides a reasonable interpretation, not to cancel the old treaty. This is the established policy of both governments, and we are only carrying it out from our own standpoint. (2) The work of the committee is limited to on-site surveys, investigation on the ground, in other words, just investigation. The majority decisions in the meeting only represent the opinions of the majority of the commissioners on factual matters, not that 'once a decision is made, the boundary line is set.' The power of 'delimitation' still lies in the direct consultations between the two governments afterwards and has nothing to do with the current work of the committee. The report of the committee has considerable weight, but it cannot bind the negotiations between the two governments. As for 'demarcation' (setting up stakes), it is even after 'delimitation.' The committee has no right to do this, needless to say. Last year, reports said that our team and the British team had erected boundary stakes in several places, which are purely unreasonable rumors. Moreover, the entire area of the undemarcated southern section, from the Nantin River in the north to the Nanma River in the south, has no formal boundary stakes. As for the three stone piles privately erected by Qing Dynasty boundary officials Liu Wansheng and Chen Can with the British officer Scott, I declared my rejection of them during last year's meeting, and the chairman decided to cancel them. Therefore, there are no boundary lines in the area, let alone boundary stakes. This session of the border demarcation work is scheduled to begin at the end of the year and will be completed before the rainy season next spring. After I arrive in Kunming, I will lead my staff directly to the border area to meet with the British commissioners and the neutral chairman in Bangsang. The first meeting is scheduled to be held on January 1, 1937. However, the work of this session is even more difficult than before. I feel a great responsibility, and I hope the people of the country will not abandon us and will give us advice from time to time. I would be deeply honored," and so on.

Guangdong Bank's Shanghai Branch Ordered to Resume Business on a Fixed Date; Raised Sufficient Registered Capital of 8 Million Hong Kong Dollars; Half of the Deposits to be Converted into Shares, the Remainder to be Repaid in Five Years 101

According to the Hua Dong News Agency, the closure of Guangdong Bank on September 4th last year had a significant social impact, and the movement to resume business had been brewing for a long time. Recently, with the assistance of Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Council, and the financial community, it was reorganized in Hong Kong on the 14th of this month. A new shareholders' meeting was convened, and Song Ziwen was elected as chairman of the board, with Wu Tiecheng, Deng Mianren, Huo Zhitong, etc. as managing directors, and Sun Ke, Hu Bijian, Huo Baoshu, Lao Jingxiu, Tang Haian, Song Zi'an, etc. as directors, actively preparing for the resumption of business.

Shanghai Branch Opens Simultaneously

Before its closure, the bank was a hub for financial institutions of overseas Chinese in South China and Southeast Asia. Branches were set up at home and abroad, including the Hong Kong head office, as well as branches in Shanghai, Hankou, Guangzhou, Taishan, Bangkok, and San Francisco, USA. These branches closed simultaneously last year. Recently, the Hong Kong head office has decided to resume business on the 23rd. The Shanghai branch has also received a telegram ordering it to resume business simultaneously on that day. The manager of the Shanghai branch is still Zhang Rongpu, and Liang Guanliu is the assistant manager. The branch has been prepared, and some employees have returned to work as usual. It is reported that branches in Yuehan and Bangkok San Francisco and other places will also open simultaneously.

Method of Repaying Deposits

According to sources at the Hua Dong News Agency, the bank's original deposits in all branches amounted to 9 million Hong Kong dollars (calculated with interest up to the date of closure last year). It had been agreed with creditors that half of the amount, approximately 4.5 million yuan, would be used as new share capital, and the remaining half would be issued as unsecured debt notes, to be repaid in five installments, once a year, each time paying one-fifth, without interest. The first repayment date is within one year after the resumption of business.

Agricultural and Commercial Bank Plans to Establish a National Agricultural Warehouse Network; Cooperates with Provinces, Cities, and Counties; The Bureau Provides Guidance and Assistance 102

Since its establishment, the Agricultural and Commercial Bank has planned to establish a national agricultural warehouse network to regulate agricultural production and facilitate the flow of agricultural funds, in order to coordinate the marketing of agricultural products nationwide, balance agricultural prices, and regulate food supply. It plans to establish large-scale cooperative warehouses in terminal markets with convenient land and water transportation, and smaller food warehouses in agricultural product distribution markets or towns and villages in the production areas. It has decided to cooperate with provincial, city, and county governments. A reporter from the New News Agency has obtained the following outline of the plan from banking circles: Cooperation methods: (1) For large-scale warehouses aimed at coordinating the marketing of agricultural products nationwide, balancing agricultural prices, and regulating the national food supply, the Bureau (Agricultural and Commercial Bank) plans to set up and operate them. Local provincial and municipal governments may participate in the investment, but their investment amount should not exceed 40% of the total capital. (2) For smaller warehouses aimed at regulating rural finance, facilitating the marketing of agricultural products, and stabilizing agricultural prices, provincial, city, and county governments plan to set up and operate them. The construction funds for the warehouses can be provided by the Bureau by 40%, but provincial, city, and county governments must reliably guarantee the repayment of principal and interest in installments. (3) For provincial, city, and county governments that establish agricultural warehouses, the required storage and mortgage funds can be provided by the Bureau as appropriate, but provincial, city, and county governments must reliably guarantee the repayment of principal and interest. (4) Upon request from provincial, city, and county governments that establish agricultural warehouses, the Bureau can send personnel to assist in the design and training of agricultural warehouse management personnel. (5) Detailed methods for the Bureau to assist provincial, city, and county governments in setting up agricultural warehouses will be negotiated and determined separately by the Bureau and provincial, city, and county governments.

Yangtze River Water Level Drops Again; Large Vessels are Suspended; Japan Shipping Company's Luoyang Maru Has Suspended Navigation; Ocean Vessels on the Upper Reaches are Blocked; There is Concern that Further Water Level Drops Will Lead to Interrupted Navigation 103

The Yangtze River water level has been declining even more in recent days, and the Yangtze River shipping business of the six companies has been severely hindered. Yesterday, the various shipping companies in this port received telegrams from Hankou stating that the water level in the Hankou-Jiujiang section has dropped to 11 feet 5 inches (including the draft). River vessels traveling upstream and downstream are only allowed to load cargo to 11 feet and must not exceed the limit. The six companies have all implemented reductions in cargo loads. For example, river vessels that can normally carry 1,500 tons can now only load a maximum of 650 tons. Vessels with an empty draft of 12 feet are all suspended from sailing. The Japan Shipping Company has decided to suspend the navigation of its large river vessel Luoyang Maru. Furthermore, the ocean vessels that sailed from Shanghai and Haizhou to Hankou, Yuezhou, and other places in early October to transport coal and salt have been unable to sail downstream due to the sharp drop in water levels. More than a dozen vessels are effectively blocked and stopped on the upper reaches. If the water level continues to decline, there is a risk that navigation on the upper reaches will be interrupted. At that time, cargo transportation will have to rely on barges. The six companies are all preparing remedial measures. Yesterday, a telegram from Yichang reported that the water level in Shashi has dropped to 6 feet, making it difficult for larger vessels to navigate. Therefore, the six companies have agreed to increase the shallow water fee for the Yangtze River (i.e., Shanghai to Hankou) by 25% and the fee for Hankou to Yichang (i.e., the middle Yangtze River, including Shashi) by 50%, effective from the first of next month. The announcement has been made to all passengers.

Page 11

The Toyota Factories Labor Dispute Has Not Been Resolved; Strikes Have Resumed at Factories in Shanghai and Other Places; All Workers at the Numbers One and Two Nei Wai Cotton Mills Have Also Gone on Strike; A Large Number of Workers Arrested for Allegedly Instigating the Labor Unrest —The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Expedite Mediation— 104

According to Da Gong News Agency, after the labor strike at the Toyota yarn factory in western Shanghai, all the workers at the Numbers 1, 2, 5, 6, and 7 Nei Wai Cotton Mills also went on strike last night. Strikes have been resumed in the Shanghai Numbers 2 and 3 and Tong Xing Number 2 Factories in the eastern Shanghai district. Labor unrest is also about to occur at the Ri Hua and Xi He Factories. The Municipal Government has ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to properly handle the labor unrest at the Japanese-owned yarn factories as quickly as possible. The labor dispute at the British-owned New Ewo Sack Factory has been resolved. The details are as follows:

The Two Toyota Factories Continue to Strike

Following the joint strike by more than 4,500 male and female workers at the Number 1 and 2 Toyota Factories, Japanese-owned factories located near Caogaodu Zhongshan Road Bridge in western Shanghai, which began on the evening of the 17th, the workers had not returned to work as of last night. Along the road in front of the two factories, in addition to the Chinese police and concession detectives stationed there, there were four or five Japanese marine corps soldiers on guard. Two armored vehicles were stationed inside the factories. According to Katsuiti Mizumura, the personnel section chief of the factory, who spoke to the Da Gong News Agency reporter who visited, the factory did not know about the workers' strike in advance, and the workers did not make any demands, which goes against the normal logic of a strike. Furthermore, the workers also destroyed the workshop of the Number 2 Factory during the strike, resulting in significant losses. Even if the workers return to work, the factory will need to be reorganized for a considerable period of time before it can start operating, he said.

The Unrest is Spreading in the Nei Wai Factories

At the Numbers 1 and 2 Nei Wai Cotton Mills on Robison Road in western Shanghai, a total of more than 3,200 day and night shift workers, at 4:00 p.m. yesterday, 1,600 workers from the weaving and spinning departments of the day shift stopped working voluntarily, causing disputes with the foremen. The factory was unable to stop them and released all the male and female workers on the day shift. At 5:30 p.m., the female workers of the night shift, influenced by the propaganda of the Japanese workers, also joined the strike. On Xiaoshadu Road and Robison Road, near the Nei Wai Cotton Mills, there were more than 3,000 male and female workers standing on the road and sidewalks, watching each other. The factory was closed tightly. It was not until 7:15 p.m. that the police from the Xiaoshadu Road Police Station and the Caogaodu Public Security Sub-bureau and the Robison Road Police Station combined their efforts to disperse them. As for the Numbers 5, 6, and 7 Nei Wai Cotton Mills on Yichang Road, only two-thirds of the Japanese workers went to work. Due to the impact of the strike at the Numbers 1 and 2 Factories, except for a small number of workers in the weaving department who went to work, the workers in the spinning department of the night shift have all gone on strike. There has been no movement at the Numbers 3 and 4 Nei Wai Cotton Mills and the Number 8 Factory on Gordon Road and the Number 9 Factory on Dagok Road.

Workers' Meeting Proposes Conditions

More than 300 workers from various Japanese-owned Nei Wai factories held a representatives' conference at 9:00 a.m. yesterday in the playground of a primary school in a people's new village on Zhongshan Road. In addition to appointing eight group leaders to direct the actions of the factories, they also proposed five conditions, which were unanimously passed as follows: (1) Increase wages by 20%; (2) Workers may not be dismissed without reason; (3) Dismissed workers shall be allowed to return to work; (4) Abolish workship laboring, restore original bounty laboring; (5) Each factory shall elect 20 representatives, and a total of 120 representatives from the factories shall elect 16 general representatives to be responsible for negotiating with the factory. If the factory dismisses the representatives, all the workers in the factories shall provide assistance. After an hour and a half, Tan Baoshou, the director of the Caogaodu Sub-bureau, heard the news and immediately led a large number of police to rush to the scene to persuade them to disperse.

The Municipal Government Orders the Social Affairs Bureau to Mediate

Regarding the outbreak of labor unrest at the Toyota yarn factory and other factories, the Municipal Government is very concerned. In order to resolve the unrest as soon as possible, it has ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to find ways to properly mediate and resolve the dispute. Currently, Pan, the director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, has instructed the Third Section to send Zhu Guilun and Zhang Chuqiang, and the General Labor Union has sent Wan Banghe to investigate the labor unrest. It is planned to summon the persons in charge and representatives of the striking factories for questioning first, and then conduct formal mediation to resolve the labor unrest as soon as possible.

Strikes Break Out Again in Shanghai Tong Xing

The workers at the Japanese-owned Shanghai Numbers 2 and 3 Factories at Guangxin Wharf on Yangshupu Road, in order to demand a general wage increase, put forward five conditions and first launched a joint strike on the evening of the 8th of this month, which lasted for four days. The factory then agreed with the foremen of each department to increase wages by 5%. After being persuaded by party and government agencies, all the workers reluctantly returned to work on the 12th. However, since the workers returned to work, the factory has not issued a formal announcement acknowledging the wage increase. The workers believe that the factory is deceiving them, so at 11:00 p.m. on the 18th, all the night shift workers suddenly announced a strike while working and left the factory. Furthermore, the Tong Xing Number 2 Factory on Yangshupu Road also experienced a labor strike yesterday morning. The inside story of this second strike is very complicated.

A Large Number of Male and Female Workers Arrested

When the night shift at the Shanghai Numbers 2 and 3 Factories went on strike, the Great Western Road Police Station sent a large number of detectives to suppress them. Zhang Linzhen and 10 other workers in the spinning room were arrested on the spot on suspicion of instigating the labor unrest and detained that night. At about 8:00 a.m. yesterday morning, about 800 male and female workers petitioned the Great Western Road Police Station, demanding their release. The police station refused the request, saying that further investigation was needed. At noon, 18 more workers were arrested at the factory, and four workers were also arrested at the Tong Xing Number 2 Factory. All of them were transferred to the Special District Court for handling.

The Japan Textile Federation is Very Concerned

Funatsu, the chairman of the Japan Textile Industry Association in China, told the Da Gong News Agency reporter that the association is very concerned about the outbreak of labor unrest in the factories in the western Shanghai district. When the problems in western Shanghai have not been resolved, strikes have broken out again in factories in Shanghai and other places, which are shaking the future of the Japanese-owned yarn industry. At a time when the operating profit this year has improved, this unfortunate incident has occurred, and it is not difficult to understand who is directing and instigating it. The association, as a yarn industry group, will certainly do its best to eliminate this labor unrest as soon as possible to maintain the development of our country's industry in China, he said.

The Labor Dispute at the British-Owned Ewo Factory Has Been Resolved

More than 300 workers at the British-owned New Ewo yarn factory sack factory on Weituoma Road, Yangshupu, put forward seven demands to the factory, including wage demands. The factory refused to accept them, which caused a strike. The Municipal General Labor Union sent its cadre Fang Banghe to contact the factory, and the representative Zhang Rongsheng from Baotou, and a satisfactory result was achieved. All the workers returned to work last night.

Japanese Marines Stationed at Various Factories

The Japanese Marine Corps, at the request of the Ri Hua, Gong Da, Nei Wai Cotton, Xi He, Shanghai Numbers 1, 4, 5, 6, Tong Xing, Yu Feng, Dong Hua, and Gong Da Number 2 Factories in the western Shanghai district and the eastern Shanghai district, dispatched a large number of soldiers, more than 500 in total, to various factories yesterday morning to be stationed there for protection. The police station and the Public Security Bureau have also sent more police officers to be closely guarded near the factories to prevent any incidents.

Li Shizeng Returned to Shanghai from Peiping Yesterday 105

Mr. Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Committee who visited Zhang Jingjiang and attended the memorial service for Duan, left Shanghai at the beginning of the month to go to Peiping and Tianjin for official business and to inspect the local situation. He recently traveled south and stayed in Beijing for a short time before taking the 11:00 p.m. express train from Beijing the night before yesterday. He arrived in Shanghai at about 7:00 a.m. yesterday morning and returned to the World College on Ferguson Road. After resting for a while, he went to visit Zhang Jingjiang and other friends to talk. At noon, he went to the Duan residence on Avenue Joffre to pay his respects.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Amendment to Grain Storage Method 108

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Executive Yuan in Nanjing: On the 18th of this month, we received a telegram from the Zhejiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation stating that the General Outline of Local Grain Storage Methods, revised and passed by the Executive Yuan in its 287th meeting, comprehensively considers national and people's livelihoods. The methods are extremely strict and the standards are exceptionally fair. During this time of national crisis, grain storage is an essential policy to be implemented, and our merchants naturally cannot shirk their responsibility. However, upon examining Article 16 of the original outline, the fundraising method stipulates that the collection should be based on the ratio of field tax, business tax, house tax, and other property income, striving for simplicity and fairness. Upon close inspection, including business tax as one of the items seems to place an excessively heavy burden on merchants, which does not fully align with the principles of simplicity and fairness. Moreover, assessing it based on the ratio of other property income is also inevitably uneven. Our Chamber has already telegraphed the Executive Yuan, requesting appropriate amendments to the original outline. All fundraising from merchants for grain storage donations should be based on the net profit of business operations, as stipulated in the last paragraph of Article 16, concerning the ratio of other property income, so as to be more adaptable to other fundraising standards. We request its adoption and prompt reconsideration, to establish sound regulations and ensure fairness." They also requested a unanimous agreement to pass the matter. It is noted that preparing grain for famine relief, and utilizing it for the development of rural production when necessary, is an essential local policy. However, when the funds allocated under the provincial, municipal, and county income items are insufficient, they may be raised through fundraising. The fundraising standard is based on the ratio of field tax, business tax, house tax, and other property income. The term "business tax" undoubtedly refers to merchants. Merchants themselves pay business tax in their commercial locations, and various taxes and levies are imposed on the transportation and sale of goods. If the grain storage donation is collected based on business turnover, the burden will inevitably be too heavy. The Federation proposes to base the fundraising on the net profit of business operations, according to the provisions of the last paragraph of Article 16 of the General Outline of Grain Storage Methods, which concerns the ratio of other property income. This is a fair proposal. It is appropriate to telegraph this to the esteemed Executive Yuan, requesting its adoption and amendment of Article 16 of the General Outline, as it would be both fair and convenient. Respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Zhejiang Silk Control Association Borrows 400,000 Yuan, China and Communications Banks Each Lend 200,000 109

The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Committee, due to the impact of weather on this year's autumn silkworm harvest, resulting in a significant reduction in yield and causing cocoon prices to soar in various regions with demand exceeding supply, has decided to increase spring silkworm eggs to meet the needs of various regions and develop the silk industry, in order to distribute them in large quantities for hatching in various regions. However, the spring silkworm eggs produced domestically next spring are insufficient to meet the distribution needs of various regions. As a remedial measure, they have borrowed 400,000 yuan from the China and Communications Banks to order 800,000 sheets of spring silkworm eggs from abroad. According to a reporter from the New News Agency, it was learned from the Bank of China that the 800,000 sheets of spring silkworm eggs ordered by the Zhejiang Silk Control Committee cost 7.5 jiao per sheet, totaling 600,000 yuan. In addition to the 200,000 yuan supplemented from the profits of the Committee's sale of spring silkworm silk, there is still a shortfall of 400,000 yuan. As a result, they consulted with Jin Runquan, the manager of the Hangzhou branch of the Bank of China. Jin came to Shanghai to request approval from the head office. The China and Communications Banks each assumed 200,000 yuan of the loan. The loan agreement has been signed, with an interest rate of 9%, using the silkworm eggs as collateral. It is expected that the principal and interest will be repaid in full when the spring cocoons are available on the market next year.

Xi'an Siege 10th Anniversary Commemoration, Public Memorial Ceremony Preparatory Committee Circular Telegram 111

"To the Shanghai Songhu Garrison Command, Security Office, Municipal Government, and forwarded to all legal entities, newspaper offices, and military units: The siege of Xi'an in the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, from mid-April to November 28th of that year, lasted eight months before the siege was lifted. Tens of thousands of soldiers and civilians died. In those times, ammunition was exhausted, and aid was cut off. Even porridge was insufficient, and people resorted to eating grass, boiling leather, and consuming oil residue. Yet, with one heart, day and night, they fought valiantly, vowing to never surrender, finally preserving the famous city and consolidating the revolutionary base in the Northwest, contributing to the success of the Northern Expedition. The tragic and heroic circumstances were unprecedented in our Party's revolutionary warfare. The people of Shaanxi Province hold a memorial ceremony every year on this day to never forget. This year marks the tenth anniversary of the memorial ceremony, coinciding with the daily worsening of foreign aggression and the severity of the national crisis. It is universally believed that only by promoting the martyrs can we encourage future generations, and only by honoring the fallen can we inspire morale. Therefore, a meeting has been convened to prepare for an expanded ceremony. We respectfully request memorial writings to highlight past achievements and uplift people's hearts, so that the red blood and loyal hearts may be further emphasized through eloquent words, and the deeds of loyalty and martyrdom may provide endless inspiration. We respectfully submit this telegram for your consideration. Respectfully, the Preparatory Committee for the Tenth Anniversary Commemoration and Public Memorial Ceremony of the Xi'an Siege."

Social Affairs Bureau Orders Factories to Quickly Establish Factory Regulations 114

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, considering that there are thousands of factories in the city, but very few have established factory regulations and submitted them for record, which often leads to a lack of basis in case of disputes, yesterday issued a special order to all factories that have not established factory regulations, or have established them but not submitted them, to quickly draft and submit them for approval. The original order stated: "According to the instructions in the Municipal Government's Order No. 2081, which approved the Ministry of Industry's Labor Document No. 5294, factory regulations are the standard for factories' treatment of workers, and are of great importance to workers' welfare and industrial production. All factories should carefully establish them for compliance. Supervisory authorities should not allow factories to freely establish regulations or summarily approve them upon submission, as this can easily lead to malpractices. Previously, this Ministry collected factory regulations from various regions, and their contents often did not comply with the Factory Law and related laws, especially in the regulations concerning 'working hours,' 'holidays,' 'death benefits,' 'termination of contracts,' 'wage payment,' and 'apprentices' food, lodging, medical, and allowance.' Moreover, the number of factory regulations that have not been submitted to the supervisory authorities for approval is very large, and even those that have been submitted for approval still have a few that conflict with the law. This is not in compliance with Article 75 of the Factory Law. Hereafter, these regulations must be strictly reviewed in accordance with the Factory Law and its related laws, and all factories that have not submitted their regulations for review must quickly draft and submit them for approval in accordance with the law, to emphasize the law and benefit labor. In addition to distribution, please investigate and instruct compliance.' In accordance with this, the Bureau is ordered to comply immediately and instruct compliance. Considering that there are thousands of factories in this city, and only a few have established factory regulations and submitted them to this Bureau for approval in accordance with the law, labor disputes often arise due to the lack of legal factory regulations as a basis. As a result of the foregoing orders, you are ordered to comply. All factories in this city that have not established factory regulations, or have established them but not submitted them, should quickly draft and submit them for approval in accordance with the law, to emphasize the law and benefit labor. This order, totaling more than one thousand nine hundred yuan."

Taikoo and Six Other Companies Announce Increased Shallow Water Fee for Cargo 117

Since the alliance of Taikoo and six other companies, it has been quite effective. Due to the shallow water level in the Yangtze River and slower navigation, a 25% increase in the shallow water fee was implemented on October 19th for cargo loaded from Hankou to Changsha and Xiangtan, and a 15% increase for cargo from Hankou to Shashi and Yichang. Now, the six companies must increase the shallow water fee again, based on water levels. The announcement from the six companies is as follows: Taikoo Navigation Company, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Jardine Matheson, Ning Shao Company, San Pei Company, and Nisshin Company announce that from December 1st, 1936, all cargo loaded from Shanghai to Wuhu and above, or from Wuhu upstream to Hankou, must be subject to a 25% shallow water fee based on water levels. Furthermore, from December 1st, 1936, all cargo loaded from Hankou to Yichang must be subject to a 50% shallow water fee based on water levels. This announcement is hereby made.

Violently Collides with Six Boats, Girl and Boatmen Tragically Drown, Losses to Six Boats Are Substantial 119

The Jardine Matheson Company's Shenguang Steamer, at approximately 9:00 PM the night before, entered Shanghai harbor and docked at the Sanpei Company's Hongsheng Wharf at Laiyi Ferry in Pudong. At that time, the tide was quite strong, and as the ship was mooring alongside the wharf, the hull was buffeted by the tide, making it difficult to control. It violently collided with the Shenyou Steamer, which was moored at the southern end of the wharf. Six wharf boats were moored on the outer side of that steamer. The outermost boat, No. 6600, carrying 90 bags of white rice, bore the brunt of the impact. The entire boat, including the cargo, was overturned and the rice sank to the bottom of the river. Several boatmen fell under the overturned boat and were unable to climb out. The second boat, No. 4930, carrying 60 bags of rice, was overturned in succession due to the impact from the first boat, and the rice also sank to the bottom of the river. Several boatmen also fell under the boat. The third boat, No. 8640, had its scull shed frame and rudder frame crushed. The fourth boat, No. 8176, had its hull planks and stern corners crushed and damaged, and water entered. The fifth boat, No. 6222, had its guardrail broken. The innermost [sixth] boat had its scaffolding broken. It is evident that the force of the Shenguang Steamer's impact was violent. The estimated loss to the cargo of each boat is approximately ten thousand yuan. The Chinese police from the Customs Water Police Station immediately used axes to cut open the bottoms of the first and second outermost overturned boats, rescuing several boatmen. However, Chen Shunquan's daughter Miaoying, the boat owner of the first boat, who was only [blank] years old, and Zhang Gougou, a boatman from Chongming on the second boat, tragically drowned and sank. Their bodies have not yet surfaced as of last night. After the Shenguang Steamer caused the accident, it continued to dock at the wharf to unload cargo as usual. The owners of the damaged boats reported the incident to the Water Police Station yesterday morning to file a claim for compensation from the steamer company.

Sending Warships to Sound the Huangpu River 120

Zeng Yangfu, the director of the Huangpu Commercial Port Preparatory Office, has noted that the depth of the Pearl River estuary is decreasing daily, making it difficult for deeper-draft vessels to enter and exit, greatly affecting commerce in the Huangpu area. Therefore, he has requested the Naval Ministry's Hydrographic Office to send warships to sound the river for dredging purposes. As a result, the office has dispatched the Gong Sheng survey vessel and technical personnel to conduct sounding operations from the Lingdingyang waters of the Pearl River estuary to the Huangpu section, which is expected to be completed within one year.

Corpse Burial Case at the Women's Hospital: Chen Xiaobao Also Files an Appeal, Explaining Reasons for Disagreeing with the Original Verdict, Claiming At Most Accessory to the Crime 122

Zhang Wenhua, a doctor at the Zhaofeng Road Hongkou Women's Hospital, and his mistress Chen Dabao (also known as Liang Meiyu), were arrested by the Huishan Police for strangling to death a woman named Lu Aili who underwent an abortion and a man named Yu Gengsheng on September 4th of this year, and burying their bodies underground. They were handed over to the First Special Court. After interrogation, Zhang was sentenced to death and Chen to life imprisonment. Zhang Wenhua, dissatisfied with the verdict, hired lawyer Yu Enliang to draft a petition to the Second Branch of the High Court.

to file an appeal.

Details have already been recorded in this newspaper. It is now known that the female convict Chen Xiaobao is also dissatisfied with the verdict and has hired lawyer Li Zhongwen to draft a petition to the Second Branch of the High Court, stating her appeal. The reasons for the appeal are roughly as follows: The First Instance Judgment in this case charges the appellant Chen Xiaobao with joint responsibility, which is based solely on the fact that the appellant was present and participated a little when the killings occurred. Being present is one thing, and participating is another. The appellant does not deny being present, but as for participating, the facts are already

insufficient to prove,

and Zhang Wenhua has not implicated the appellant. Therefore, this point is really worth studying. Examining Zhang Wenhua's confessions, although there are slight inconsistencies, the actual course of events at the time can be roughly presumed. The deceased, Yu and Lu, went to the Hongkou Obstetrics Hospital to request an abortion. Zhang Wenhua was careless during the operation and cut Lu's uterus, causing internal bleeding and death. Fearing that Yu would make a fuss, Zhang tricked him into having blood drawn and killed him. The cause of death was

air leaking into the blood,

or an injection of a heavy dose of anesthesia. Zhang Wenhua's confessions are contradictory on this point, but the main cause of death was the injection. The Hongkou Obstetrics Hospital is run solely by Zhang Wenhua. The appellant is only a nurse and has virtually no medical knowledge. However, during the operation, she passed on the necessary items from the side. She had no right to question or participate in Zhang's surgery. Zhang Wenhua performed the abortion on Lu, and the

surgical error

was naturally something the appellant could not have known beforehand. Therefore, Lu's death was due to surgical error, and Yu's death was due to Zhang's conspiracy. The First Instance's statement of "participating from beginning to end" is arbitrary. As for whether Yu and Lu died from the abortion, the injection, or strangulation, it is not difficult to determine medically, as the circumstances of a living person being strangled and a dead person being strangled are clearly different. Moreover, according to legal principles, the cause of the crime should be based on the most important cause. In this case, Lu's

uterus was already ruptured,

leaving no hope of life. Yu was injected with a heavy dose of poison, also leaving no hope of life. Therefore, even if the fact of strangling with a towel existed, it cannot aggravate the crime, and the absence of it cannot mitigate the responsibility. It has no causal relationship with the deaths of Yu and Lu. Stepping back, even if Zhang informed the appellant beforehand of his plan to murder Yu after the abortion went wrong, the appellant, being a concubine, was completely under his control. Being a woman with limited knowledge, she would naturally lose her reason and judgment upon suddenly learning of the

impending disaster.

She could only obey in everything. This was due to her position and circumstances. Anyone else in her position would have done the same. How can one solely blame a woman with limited knowledge like the appellant? Therefore, considering the circumstances, the appellant's situation was extremely helpless. It is understandable to fault her for being weak and indecisive, but to say that she had a joint intention is not understanding. As for the subsequent

concealment of the corpses,

she was forced into this and had no other choice. Reporting her husband was something human nature could not allow. And if the corpses were not concealed, what else could be done? Regardless of moral principles and focusing solely on actions, it was only post-facto assistance, at most an accessory to the crime. However, the First Instance judged the appellant as a joint offender, which seems excessive in both law and reason. Therefore, she requests that the original verdict be overturned and a lawful judgment be made.

Woman Commits Suicide by Poisoning, Suicide Note Found Nearby, Writing, "Injustice Sunk to the Bottom of the Sea, When Will It Be Redressed?" Sent to Hospital for Treatment, Condition Very Critical 123

A female guest, claiming to be Zhang Chenshi, arrived at the Chunjiang Inn on Shandong Road in the Public Concession a few days ago. She was about thirty years old and checked into room 44. Late at night the previous evening, she committed suicide by ingesting opium, groaning in bed. The next morning, the tea boy discovered her. He informed the Old Zha Police Station, which sent an ambulance to take her to Renji Hospital for injections and treatment. She had taken a large amount of poison and it is unknown whether her life can be saved. A suicide note was found nearby, running to thousands of words, detailing her grievances. It was written, "Injustice sunk to the bottom of the sea, when will it be redressed?" The content was roughly that Ms. (Zhang Chenshi claimed to be) was from Baoshan. Since childhood, she was married through a matchmaker to Zhang Zhendong, a fellow townsman who runs the Tongtai Seafood Store in the Nanshi. They were married for more than ten years and had four children, of whom only one daughter, Wei Yong, now eleven years old, survives. Her husband's business had flourished in recent years and he had become rich, so he sought pleasure and married Hu Laosan, an undercover prostitute from Jiangyin, also known as Hu Xiufen, on the outside. Ms. Zhang Chenshi found out and questioned her husband, which aroused his suspicion. He colluded with his master, Sun Luling, to design all sorts of ways to force her to divorce. After being kicked out, she was pregnant and her husband still wanted to kill her. Having no other choice, she had to seek her own death to end her life. The situation is very tragic.

Young Woman Grieves Husband's Death, Suffers Nervous Breakdown, Commits Suicide, First Injects Herself with Ten Doses of Morphine, Then Swallows a Bottle of Sleeping Pills 124

Li Heshi, a Cantonese woman aged twenty-two, residing at No. 12, Si Cheng Li, Julaida Road in the French Concession, was a obstetrician at He Ruizhen Obstetrics Hospital, No. 1, Qiqing Lane, Xin Guangdong Street, Qujiang Road, Hongkou. Her husband, Li Liang (also Cantonese and a doctor), worked at the Guangdong Hospital in Nanjing. After he died of illness a month ago, Ms. Li, saddened by her husband's death and her young widowhood, became depressed and suffered a nervous breakdown. She suddenly became tired of life. On the night of the 16th, Ms. Li first injected herself with a box of morphine needles, a total of ten, at home, but the anesthetic was ineffective. She then swallowed a bottle of sleeping pills and became unconscious. The next morning (17th) at 8:00 AM, her mother, He Wangshi (44 years old, Cantonese), called her to get up. When she didn't respond, she discovered the suicide and sent her to the Red Cross General Hospital on Haige Road. However, she had taken too much poison and efforts to save her were ineffective. She died at 11:30 AM on the 18th. The hospital informed the French Police, who sent investigators to investigate. The body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for autopsy. Yesterday, a report was submitted to the Special Court. Inspector Wang Ren and a forensic doctor arrived at the scene. It was determined that the deceased died of poisoning. The body was handed over to the deceased's mother, He Wangshi, for burial.

Police Chief Major Faber and his staff welcomed him into the building. Mr. Nazia got out of the car to a grand ceremony. Two teams of Russian and Vietnamese police and a special Chinese police team stood on either side, led by Chief Officer Gu Cai, saluting with their guns. At the same time, the police band played the French national anthem to express their welcome. Mr. Nazia paid close attention to all departments of the Police Department, especially the Secretariat, Political Office, Detective Office, Complaints Department, Fingerprint Section, and Wireless Telegraph Alarm Department. The police authorities also demonstrated an alarm exercise. All participating detectives were well-trained and very agile. Mr. Nazia praised them highly. Afterwards, he visited the Municipal Council, where he was personally greeted by Director-General Wei Zhiren and Director Fu Lesi, among others. He was guided to visit the various departments and was briefed on the current status of various tasks. Mr. Nazia expressed his satisfaction.

Dada and Datong Launch Shanghai-Nantong Short Route Starting Yesterday 126

The Dada Datong Shipping Company of the Tongyang Line, in view of the shallow waters during the winter season, the scheduled voyages often arrive in Nantong early, late at night, or the next morning. To facilitate passengers, it was decided through consultation to launch a short-route express between Shanghai and Xin'gang. The route passes through Langshan Port, Yao Port, Dasheng, and Zhangyin Port, and the Dahe of Dada Company and the Zhida of Datong Company have been assigned to run this route. The boats will depart from Shanghai and Tiansheng Port at 12:00 noon every day, arriving on the same day. Shanghai and Nantong began this operation yesterday. Yesterday at noon, the Dada Company's Dahe left Shanghai. Today at noon, the Datong Company's Zhida leaves Shanghai. All prices remain the same and there is no increase. Passengers have called it convenient.

Municipal Council Rejects Small Taxi Cabs 128

The operation of small rental cars and taxicabs in the Public Concession was once considered in the spring of last year, but it failed to materialize due to the opposition of the police authorities. Recently, a merchant raised the issue again and submitted it to the Municipal Council. The plan was to operate small rental cars, with each car equipped with a road meter to charge passengers. If the results are good, they plan to establish stations in the central area, where passengers can hail the cars along the way. The estimated fare is about half that of the current large rental cars. This matter was recently discussed in detail by the Police Committee of the Municipal Council. The Chief of the Police Department and the Director of the Donation Office presented their opinions. The Chief of the Police Department stated that although these small cars are structurally sound, they are not suitable for the traffic situation in this city. There is a conflict with the existing car rental industry, and future competition may lead to mutual losses. Furthermore, small cars may not be as convenient as rickshaws in terms of road space. The Director of the Donation Office also stated that the Public Concession authorities have always disapproved of small rental cars and taxicabs. This is why the current car rental business exists. This business has a large investment. If the Municipal Council allows small rental cars to appear on the market, the public should be given adequate preparation beforehand to avoid losses to the current car rental merchants. At a recent meeting of the Municipal Council, due to the continued opposition of the Chief of the Police Department, the authorities considered that there were many obstacles and decided to reject the proposal. Therefore, small rental cars and taxicabs will not appear on the market for the time being.

Li Hongyi's Grandson, Guo Chao, Meets Enemy Who Assassinated Li 129

The Japanese newspaper, "Japanese Daily News," reported that Li Guochao, the 31-year-old grandson of the late Qing Dynasty official Li Hongyi, traveled to Japan on the 2nd of this month to investigate ancient pottery, paintings, precious metals, and works of art. He returned to Shanghai on the 18th and made the following statement: "I don't really know my grandfather, but I have heard about my grandfather's negotiations with Japan. However, as his grandson, I wanted to learn more about Japan, so I made a trip to Japan. I stayed in Tokyo, Osaka, Kobe, and Kyoto for two weeks. I met all the people who were related to my grandfather and was treated kindly. Mr. Oyama Toyotaro, the enemy who assassinated my grandfather in Yamaguchi Prefecture in the 28th year of Meiji, also met with me in Tokyo. Mr. Oyama told me about what happened at that time. I was filled with emotion when I heard it."

City Federation Sends Letter to Municipal Council Urging Collection of Vacant House Tax 130

Since the French Municipal Council first implemented the collection of vacant house tax, businesses and industries have been in agreement. The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession also suggested that the Municipal Council follow suit, but this has not yet materialized. The First Special District Citizens Federation sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, urging them to implement it as soon as possible. The original letter stated, "According to a letter from the 21st Branch of our Federation, since the 'January 28th Incident' in Shanghai, all industries have been in a slump and are struggling to survive, resulting in an increasing number of vacant houses on various roads. The reason for this is that rents are too expensive, and businesses cannot afford them. Now that the French Municipal Council has determined that vacant houses affect the market and has implemented the collection of vacant house tax, our Public Concession can also follow suit. This measure will not only maintain tax revenue, but also the vacant house tax will encourage landlords to lower rents, which is a key to revitalizing the market. We hope that you will forward this letter to the Municipal Council to implement it as soon as possible for the benefit of the market."

Chen Dimin and Wife's Lawsuit Concludes: Wife Sues for Divorce, Husband Sues for Cohabitation. Both Cases Were Heard Together Yesterday and Concluded - Judgment Set for the 24th - 133

Chen Dimin, a native of Anhui who resides at No. 379, Beile Road, in the French Concession and was formerly a comprador for a foreign firm in Lafayette Village, is 40 years old this year. He married Tan Kunfan, a woman from Suzhou (also 40 years old), in his early years, and they have six children. They lived together at No. 15, Lafayette Village, Lafayette Road. Last spring, a dispute arose, and after a fight, Tan took the children and left Chen's residence, returning to her mother's home on Dagu Road. She first reported Chen's assault and injury to the French police, who prosecuted Chen in the Special No. 2 Court. The court sentenced Chen to a fine of 20 yuan, suspended for two years. Later, Tan filed a suit for separation and alimony against Chen in the civil division of the Special No. 2 Court, resulting in a settlement where Chen would pay 350 yuan per month for living expenses and an additional 20 yuan for the children. They were to live separately for four months. Recently, Chen filed a suit for cohabitation against Tan in the civil division of the Special No. 2 Court, requesting that Tan Kunfan be ordered to return home with the children and the clothes and money she had taken. Tan also filed a suit for divorce against Chen, requesting alimony of 70,000 yuan and that Chen take back the children to raise. The court, based on the pleadings, had held a hearing once, the details of which were recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Ma Yishu presided over the joint hearing of the two cases in the Civil Division No. 7. First, the divorce case was heard. According to the plaintiff, Chen Tan Kunfan, they were married in Japan in the 7th year of the Republic (1918) and have photos as proof. After returning to China, because her mother objected, they remarried at the Huizhong Hotel. Now, because the defendant has an affair and mistreats her, she requests a divorce. Regarding alimony, the defendant is wealthy and certainly has the ability to pay, and so on. The defendant, Chen Dimin, was represented by a lawyer who stated that the defendant's affair with the plaintiff was true, but the wedding photos were to deceive her mother, and there was no actual marriage. The defendant has a legal wife surnamed Zai, who passed away in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Regarding the alimony portion, Chen's property has already been mortgaged, and he is unable to pay. He is now requesting cohabitation, so there is naturally no need to pay. Moreover, the two parties were certified to have separated in the 8th year of the Republic (1919) by lawyers Heckmond and Teppick, but then continued to cohabit, and so on. He submitted the separation document as evidence and stated that Chen was willing to adopt the children. The court verified the situation, ordered a debate, and then declared the hearing concluded, setting the 24th for judgment. Then, the cohabitation case was heard. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the plaintiff's wife had passed away, the defendant had been away for a long time, and the four-month period of agreed-upon separation had expired, so the court should order the defendant to return home with the children to cohabit. The defendant, Tan Kunfan, stated that the relationship between husband and wife was completely broken and they could not cohabit. After arguments by both sides' lawyers, the court declared the debate concluded and set the 24th for judgment.

Yesterday's receipts of 752 yuan, 3 jiao, and 2 fen have not yet been included. The titles of the donating gentlemen are also omitted due to space limitations and will be published successively. We respectfully hope for your understanding. Among the industrial and commercial circles in our country, there are indeed those who accurately record the book value of their property, but there are many cases where it does not match the actual value, and the discrepancy is quite large. Now that the government's income tax is about to be implemented, if this continues without rectification, those who record values lower than the actual value will pay more taxes, affecting their business. Those who record values higher than the actual value are suspected of tax evasion, which is not permitted by law. Therefore, estimating the accuracy of original assets and obtaining appropriate proof from a third party is a matter of utmost urgency. It is said that the office has experts from various industries and accepts this kind of commission to serve the people of the country.

Car Parking Fees Revised by the French Municipal Council: Calculated According to the Area Occupied 134

The French Municipal Council, upon receiving an order from the consulate yesterday, revised the parking fees for public cars, calculated according to the size of the road area occupied by the car. Those occupying 4.5 square meters or less will pay 5 yuan per car per quarter; those occupying 4.5 to 5.5 square meters will pay 6 yuan per car per quarter; those occupying 5.5 to 6.5 square meters will pay 7 yuan per car per quarter; those occupying 6.5 to 7.5 square meters will pay 8 yuan per car per quarter; and those occupying 7.5 to 9 square meters or more will pay 9 yuan per car per quarter.

Letter 138

To the editor: Having read in your newspaper's foreign news column, "A paper box shop east of the new county jail in Dongmen Nei, Changshu, was careless, causing a fire that spread to as many as nine households, and two firefighters died. It is also reported that when the fire was raging, the prisoners in the west end rioted and one opium addict escaped," this is slightly inconsistent with the facts. On the 14th of this month (this month) at around 10:00 AM, the paper box suddenly burst into flames, and at the time of the fire, the tenants detained in this office did indeed have a situation of relying on the crowd to cause a riot in an attempt to escape. Fortunately, the members were able to protect them effectively, and no accidents occurred, and no one escaped. The report in your newspaper is probably based on an unverified interview, and I am sincerely afraid that the outside world will not understand the truth, so I have specifically written this letter to correct it, and I ask that it be published in the "Letters" column. Please give my regards to the editor of the Shenbao. Bei Ding, Custodian and Warden of Changshu County Prison, November 16th.

Dear Editor: In the second edition of the Shanghai Shenbao supplement of October 25, there was an article entitled "The Secret Communications of Lixiao," which stated that "Emperor Shunzhi of China is now revered as the ancestor by 'Lixiao'" and "Lixiao in China also has a tendency to decline day by day. This highest organization is even more out of the question," which is inconsistent with the facts. Our founder of Lixiao is Mr. Yang Lairu. Since Yang Zu founded the Yi Lixiao religion, it has been in the world for three hundred years, with the mission of saving the nation from danger and rescuing social hearts. Now Lixiao has spread all over the world, all from the same line of Yang Zu. Except for Yang Zu, there is no so-called ancestor. According to legend, Emperor Shunzhi of the former Qing Dynasty once entered Lixiao because he was touched by the development of Lixiao, which was unfavorable to the Manchu Qing regime. Therefore, he did not hesitate to join Lixiao in the hope of changing the ideological propositions of our Lixiao, but because there are so many people in Lixiao and the organization is secret, it can be said that it is rarely affected by it. The doctrines that Lixiao now believes in are as consistent as a string of coins, which is proof. Since this association was approved by the central government in the 24th year (of the Republic, 1935), it has made every effort to promote the doctrines of Lixiao and promote the work of advising against smoking and drinking. Lixiao organizations in various places are also making every effort to organize and promote it. Now that the statement is untrue, I am sincerely afraid of confusing the hearing, and I hope to be given the favor of correcting it. Please give my regards to the editor of the Shanghai Shenbao, and I wish you well. The China Lixiao General Association, November 19th.

Weather Report 139

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong, the surrounding areas, and the Yellow Sea are clear and cold, with gentle northwest to north winds. The upper and middle reaches of the Yellow River are calm and windless. The upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River have light north to northeast winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the East China Sea are cloudy, but still fine, quite cold, and have occasional north to northeast seasonal winds. The northeast wind in the Taiwan Strait is quite strong. The hurricane south of Guam Island is still moving northwest. Its center was within about 120 miles of 12 degrees north latitude and 146 degrees east longitude at 2:00 PM. The wind force is unknown. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 63.1, and the lowest was 46.9. On the same day last year, the highest was 60.4, and the lowest was 39.4.

General Situation of Commercial Changes in Shanghai in July and August This Year (Continued) (No. 38 of the General Situation of Shanghai Industry and Commerce) 141

— Chief Editor of China WeChat

3. Establishment of China Oil Lamp Company—The company was initiated by Mr. Chen Gongbo and others, with an approved capital of 150,000 yuan. It is estimated that the actual amount received has reached 80,000 to 90,000 yuan. It is a limited company organization, with Mr. Kong Yongzhi as chairman of the board and Mr. Chen Zuyi as general manager, specializing in the manufacture of various lamp oils. They have applied for a five-year patent, with the main factory located at No. 162, Lane 503, Huade Road, and a branch factory on the edge of Zhougong Temple, Santiaoshi, Tianjin. The main factory employs more than 200 workers and can produce 3,000 lamps of oil per day, with wide sales.

4. Clearance Sale of the Guangming Electric Appliance Thermos Bottle Company—The company was established in the 14th year of the Republic of China (1925), with an original capital of 180,000 yuan in national currency. It is a limited company organization, with Mr. Lei Binglin as chairman of the board and Mr. Liang Bozhi as manager. The factory is located on Qingyun Road, Zhabei, specializing in the manufacture of thermos bottle liners and glass electrical appliances. It employs more than 200 workers. In the past, the business was quite considerable, but after the January 28 Incident, the entire equipment of the factory was destroyed, resulting in huge losses. Later, after a board meeting, it was decided to reduce the capital to 112,000 yuan to reorganize and resume business. However, in the face of the current recession, it is not easy to maintain. Therefore, in May of this year, it temporarily announced a shutdown. On June 14, a shareholders' meeting resolved to sell the factory's entire property, accounts, assets, trademarks, etc., to Xinghua Company for operation. The handover was not actually carried out until this month.

The above are the important changes in the manufacturing industry in August. As for the sales aspect, the closure of the China Xingye National Goods Company is particularly noteworthy. The company only opened in April of this year and announced its liquidation after only four months of operation, which shows that it is not easy to operate industry and commerce at present. (End)
