Education News

The City's Cultural Circles Established the Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association Yesterday: Resolved to Send Telegrams of Condolence to Chairman Fu and the Frontline Soldiers, Elected Li Zhaohuan et al. as Members of the Support Association, and Passed Cultural Fundraising and慰勞Measures 142

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the city's cultural circles held a preparatory meeting at the Municipal Mass Education Center in the South City to support the soldiers suppressing bandits in Suiyuan. The meeting resolved to send telegrams of condolence to Chairman Fu and passed fundraising and 慰勞measures. It also organized and established the Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association, electing Li Zhaohuan and 61 others as members. The details are as follows:

Participating Groups

The Cultural Construction Association, Jiaotong University, Jinan University, Fudan University, Guanghua University, China Public School, Wuben Girls' High School, Jingye High School, Huadong Girls' High School, Zhengxing Girls' High School, Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, Shishi Xin Bao, Min Bao, Zhonghua Daily, Shenzhou Daily, Shang Bao, Wai Lun She, Shanghai News Agency, Guomin She, Da Gong She, Commercial Press, Zhonghua Book Company, and representatives from various cultural groups, including He Bingsong, Jiang Jianbai, Chen Jicheng, Fang Huanru, Ma Yinliang, Zai Boqi, Gu Zhizhong, Sun Mingqi, Xu Xingchu, Zhou Hanmei, Hu Lan, Huang Jingzhai, Song An, Chen Dongbai, Jin Guangmei, Zhu Zhiming, Ma Jiazhen, Xu Zexiang, Zhu Youxian, Tao Guangchuan, Wu Nanxuan, Lu Shibai, Zhou Jianyun, Yin Yiwen, Huang Zaoxiong, Gu Jiwu, Yan Kechang, and others, totaling over a hundred people, attended.

Chairman's Report

Jiang Jianbai of the Cultural Construction Association, He Bingsong of Jinan University, Chen Jicheng of China Public School, Gu Zhizhong of Xinwen Bao, and Fang Huanru of Wai Lun She were elected as the presidium, with Zhou Hanmei as the emcee and Huang Jingzhai as the recorder. After performing the formalities, Jiang Jianbai of the presidium reported that the Shanghai cultural circles are vast, and in the past, most of the patriotic work was carried out separately. Now, it is felt that there is a need to concentrate forces and unify steps. The purpose of convening this general meeting today is to organize and provide more substantial and powerful assistance to the soldiers suppressing bandits in Suiyuan, whether in material or spiritual aspects, to fulfill the national duty of saving the country, and so on. Telegrams of Condolence to Soldiers

After the Chairman's report, the proposals were discussed, and it was immediately resolved to send telegrams of condolence to the frontline soldiers. The original text is as follows: Chairman Fu of Suiyuan, and to all the officers and soldiers guarding the territory on the front line, the bandits were driven by the enemy to invade the border. Fortunately, our officers and soldiers bravely marched and fought head-on to defend our territory and demonstrate our national power. The sound of your victories spreads, and the whole country is impressed and comforted. We still hope that you will fight to the end and annihilate these ugly prisoners. This association vows to lead the entire city's cultural circles to be your strong support. In addition to actively carrying out fundraising and 慰勞 activities, we first send this telegram. We respectfully await your victory. The Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association of the Shanghai Cultural Circles, bowed.

Establishment of the Support Association

Next, the organization and establishment of the Cultural Circles Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association was discussed and approved. Li Zhaohuan, He Bingsong, Weng Zhilong, Zhan En, Ou Yuanhuai, Zhang Shouyong, Jiang Jianbai, Chen Jicheng, Hu Pu'an, Huang Bohui, Ma Yinliang, Hu Zhengzhi, Zhu Yingpeng, Sun Wuqi, Lin Baisheng, Pan Gongbi, Tong Hangbai, Xu Xingchu, Tao Baichuan, Huang Zaoxiong, Hu Lan, Liu Haisu, Lu Fei Bohong, Shen Junru, Qian Cangshuo, Zhou Feicheng, Song An, Zhu Youxian, Ma Jiazhen, Yin Yiwen, Fang Huanru, Zhang Shichuan, Li Minwei, Shao Zuiweng, Lu Shibai, Xu Zexiang, Gu Jiwu, Yao Sufeng, Tao Guangchuan, Wu Nanxuan, Fan Zhongyun, Wang Yunwu, Zhang Yi, and 61 others were elected as members. Li Zhaohuan, Wang Boqi, Ma Yinliang, Wang Yunwu, Jiang Jianbai, He Bingsong, Chen Jicheng, Tong Hangbai, Fang Huanru, Liao Maoru, and Zhou Jianyun were elected as standing members.

Fundraising and 慰勞

Finally, fundraising and 慰勞measures for the cultural circles were discussed and immediately resolved: (1) Each unit is responsible for supervising and urging fundraising, and all funds raised will be transferred to the bank; (2) Individuals will conduct fundraising and transfer the funds to the agency where they are located for transfer to the bank; (3) The association will organize a fundraising team to be responsible for supervising fundraising by profession. In addition, a savings box and patriotic gift coupons will be considered. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Comparison of the General Situation of Education at All Levels Nationwide 143

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the general situation of education at all levels nationwide over the years. Regarding higher education, because the directly administered colleges and universities are directly surveyed, the procedures are simple, and statistics have been compiled up to the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). For the school education and social education under the jurisdiction of various provinces and cities, because there are many county districts under the jurisdiction of the provinces, the procedures are time-consuming. Therefore, the survey materials for secondary education, primary education, and social education in various provinces and cities nationwide are now complete and have been completed for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Up to this month, the general situation of education at all levels nationwide and its comparison are compiled by calculating, analyzing, and comparing the educational situations at all levels that have been statistically completed by the Ministry of Education:

Cultural Circles: Support Suiyuan Movement 144

The Education Community of Jiangsu Province: All faculty and staff of schools in the provincial capital of Jiangsu, such as Zhenjiang Provincial Model School, have initiated a campaign to donate one day's salary to support the front lines. Students from various schools are also actively saving and donating generously to aid the soldiers at the front. It is also reported that provincial secondary schools throughout Jiangsu will also be making contributions.

Zhejiang University: In the past two days, faculty and students of Zhejiang University have organized fundraising groups. For faculty and staff: (1) Donating one day's salary as the minimum; (2) Additional fundraising will be conducted separately. Considering the harsh cold in Suiyuan, drawing inspiration from the Beijing academic community's initiative to donate leather clothing, funds will be used to purchase silk floss produced in Hangzhou to make silk floss vests, which will be sent to the soldiers defending the territory at the front. For students: (1) Voluntary donations, handled by the student union; students of the Agricultural College have set a minimum of one yuan per person; (2) The Agricultural College will also donate a large quantity of chrysanthemums, to be sold to raise funds. Students from the Engineering College are considering a universal one-day fast.

Soochow University: All faculty and students of Soochow University are donating funds to support the Suiyuan anti-banditry army. On November 18th, several students, along with faculty and staff, initiated fundraising. Students donate a minimum of 50 cents each, and faculty and staff donate one day's salary. Funds will be deposited at the Soochow Bank for collection and remittance to Suiyuan.

Fudan University: Since the invasion of Suiyuan by bandits and puppet troops, Fudan University has advocated thrift and expressed sympathy for the soldiers at the front. 600 yuan has already been remitted to Chairman Fu. Yesterday, 500 yuan was raised and telegraphed to Chairman Chiang.

Elementary School Teachers Association: The Shanghai Elementary School Teachers Association held a regular meeting at its premises yesterday at 4 p.m., chaired by Feng Yixian and recorded by Xi Feiyuan. Resolutions were made: (1) On how to express support for the Suiyuan issue: 1. Send a telegram to express sympathy to the soldiers at the front; 2. Send letters to all member schools to earnestly conduct fundraising to help with military supplies; 3. Petition the central government to provide substantial assistance with troops; (2) The issue of subsidies from the Municipal Council will be transferred to the Private School Advancement Association for discussion.

Shanghai University School of Commerce: The students of the journalism department of the School of Commerce at Shanghai University have initiated a fundraising campaign to support the anti-Japanese soldiers in Suiyuan. This has been reported in various newspapers and has now garnered enthusiastic support from students in other departments and the university's standing committee. It is reported that at the 30th anniversary celebration of the university last night, President Liu Zhanen delivered an impassioned speech and initiated "Sunday Movement," where all savable money every Sunday would be donated to the front lines to enable the soldiers to persevere with the enemy, thereby compensating for the shortcomings of temporary assistance. Donations were also collected on the spot during the meeting.

Shanghai College of Commerce: President Pei of the National Shanghai College of Commerce recently advocated that all faculty and staff donate one day's salary, and all students skip one meal. The commercial practice company will also enthusiastically donate one day's business revenue. It is reported that the total amount of donations will be remitted to the front lines within days.

Shanghai Provincial High School: Shanghai Provincial High School in this city, recognizing the courageous resistance of Chairman Fu and his officers and soldiers, has made an initial donation of 500 yuan by all faculty and students to be remitted to Suiyuan as aid.

Xin Huan School: Xin Huan Vocational School, Xin Huan Middle School, and Xin Huan Elementary School on Chongqing Road in this city, in light of Chairman Fu of Suiyuan leading soldiers in bravely resisting the enemy, have initiated a fundraising campaign to aid Suiyuan. All faculty and students are extremely enthusiastic.

Jiao Tong University: The student union executive committee of Jiao Tong University in this city has decided to launch a campaign to aid Suiyuan immediately, soliciting donations of cash and clothing from all faculty, staff, and students to support Suiyuan.

Suzhou Women's Normal School of Jiangsu Province: Faculty and students of Suzhou Women's Normal School of Jiangsu Province gathered on the 17th and, in addition to sending a telegram of support to the anti-banditry soldiers in eastern Suiyuan, donated over 200 yuan, which was directly telegraphed to Chairman Fu for distribution to the soldiers at the front.

Lida School: All faculty and students of Lida Academy in Jiangwan resolved that faculty and staff would contribute 5% to 15% of their monthly salaries as aid, and students would donate at least 40 cents each. Many Nanyang students at the school generously donated 5 to 10 yuan.

Minzhi Four Schools: Minzhi Journalism School, Minzhi Elementary and Middle Schools, and Minzhi Supplementary School on Baishi Road in this city held a fundraising campaign yesterday. Principal Gu Zhizhong reported and resolutions were made: (1) A four-day fundraising drive for the soldiers in eastern Suiyuan will be held from today until the 23rd; a telegram will be sent to the loyal and brave soldiers at the front lines to express sympathy; (3) Middle school students will donate at least half a day's wages and solicit donations from relatives and friends.

Four Magazine Publishers: The Chinese Stream Society, Writers' Society, Translation Society, and Literary Quarterly, along with the Three New Magazine Society, telegraphed Chairman Fu yesterday, stating: "To Chairman Fu Yisheng of the Suiyuan Provincial Government and all anti-Japanese soldiers: We express our utmost sincerity and hope that you will fight to the end for the survival and independence of the Chinese nation."

Municipal Xinlu Normal School: All faculty and students of the Municipal Xinlu Normal School launched a donation drive to express sympathy to the soldiers at the front during their memorial week this week. It is reported that all faculty and students are currently planning the drive, and funds will be remitted to the front lines as soon as they are collected.

Hangzhou Hongdao Girls' Middle School: The student union of Hangzhou Hongdao Girls' Middle School initiated a joint four-day vegetarian fast by all faculty, students, workers to donate the saved expenses in full to the front lines to comfort the soldiers resisting the enemy.

Tingxi Vocational High School: Jiangxi Vocational High School and Jiangxi Middle School, in addition to sending a telegram of encouragement, launched a thrift campaign. A sum of 150 yuan has been collected and telegraphed to Chairman Fu Zuoyi.

Peicheng Girls' Middle School: Peicheng Girls' Elementary and Middle School convened a meeting of faculty and staff yesterday afternoon and resolved to organize a Suiyuan support fundraising committee to collect 5,000 yuan to purchase silk floss vests and medical supplies to be sent to the Suiyuan front.

Ningbo Native Place Association Elementary School: All teachers of the No. 1 Elementary School of the Ningbo Native Place Association have decided to cut meals for one month and use part of the meal expenses as donations. At the same time, students will be fundraising inside and outside the school.

Loshe Rural Normal School: All faculty and students of the Provincial Loshe Rural Normal School have jointly decided to raise 300 yuan as an expression of support for the soldiers at the front. In addition to regular voluntary donations from faculty and students, meals will be reduced from the 17th to raise the insufficient amount until the 300 yuan target is reached. It is reported that, to expedite the remittance of funds, the school has found a way to advance funds and remit them to the Shanghai Shen Bao newspaper for collection and transfer.

Establishment of Midwifery or Nursing Schools Should Follow Regulations: Renhui Hospital Enrolls Students Without Authorization, Social Affairs Bureau Orders Immediate Suspension 146

Renhui Obstetrics Hospital on Haining Road in this city has not been registered with the Health Bureau, nor has it applied for approval from the Social Affairs Bureau. It has established itself and enrolled students without authorization. The Social Affairs Bureau has verified the facts and ordered the hospital to immediately stop enrolling students, dismiss existing students, and return all fees collected. It is reported that the Social Affairs Bureau has issued a separate public announcement, as many hospitals in this city are unaware of the procedures for establishing nursing or midwifery schools, that in the future, those establishing midwifery or nursing schools must comply with the revised regulations for private schools promulgated by the ministry, the revised regulations for vocational schools, and the requirements for the establishment of senior nursing vocational schools. Otherwise, they will be banned immediately.

Municipal No. 1 Sports Field: News of Industrial and Commercial Football Competition: Teams to Draw Lots to Determine Order on Sunday: 56 Participating Teams Divided into Four Groups for Competition 149

The eighth Industrial and Commercial Amateur Football Competition of the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field closed registration on October 31st. A total of 56 teams registered to participate. The field has only one football field, and the number of teams is too large to be allocated, so the newly-added Huichang team has decided not to accept. The old members of Guanshengruzhi team, totaling 56 teams, have been carefully reviewed and divided into four groups according to their skill levels: "Unity," "Congealing," "Essence," and "Spirit," with 14 teams in each group. The teams will be summoned to the field at 9 a.m. this Sunday (the 22nd) to draw lots. Each major group will be divided into two subgroups, i.e., seven teams in each group, to hold a single round-robin tournament. After the competition, the champions of the same group will be scheduled for another final to determine the winner. It is hoped that each team will send a representative (no separate letters will be sent) to the field on time to draw lots for the grouping. It is also reported that the competition will begin from 1:30 p.m. on the 27th and 28th of this month (Saturday).

Municipal Sports Meet Awards Ceremony Held Yesterday: Director Pan Represented the Mayor in Giving Instructions and Awards: Those Who Have Not Received Awards Will Be Notified Separately to Collect Them 150

The awards ceremony for the fourth Municipal Sports Meet of this city was held yesterday at 2 p.m. in the auditorium of the Municipal Government. Director Pan represented the mayor in giving instructions and awards. Participants included Section Chief Zhang, Field Director Shao, Director Wang, and more than 200 representatives from various schools. Those who have not received awards will be notified separately by the bureau to collect them. The details of the awards ceremony are recorded below.

Director's Speech: The ceremony began with Director Pan giving a speech, stating that today is the awards ceremony for the fourth Municipal Sports Meet of this city. The mayor could not attend due to other engagements and is represented by him. He had a few points to report to everyone. The conference started on October 22nd and was originally scheduled for three days. Due to too many programs, it was extended for half a day and completely ended on the morning of the 25th. Because there was no time to award prizes on the spot, the ceremony was postponed to today. A total of 1,300 athletes from 139 schools participated in the track and field competitions, and 18 teams from 14 schools participated in the group competitions. During the conference, the spirit of the athletes from various schools was still good, and no disputes occurred, which was commendable. However, there was no progress in terms of results, which is what we hope everyone will strive for. This time, many parties have donated a lot of prizes. Therefore, in addition to the team awards, individuals who score more than 5 points will receive prizes as encouragement. However, the real purpose of sports is not prizes, but to strengthen the physique and contribute to the country. Now that the national crisis is serious and the nation is facing danger, everyone should double their efforts in physical training. After the speech, the awards were presented.

Qingwu Cup Handball Tournament: Yan Peiqiu Wins Championship, Sun Baoqi Runner-up 155

The Qingwu Cup Handball Singles Championship concluded the other day. Yan Peiqiu defeated Sun Baoqi two sets to one, winning the championship. Sun took second place. Both sides were evenly matched, and the battle was full of highlights. In the first set, Sun served first and scored five consecutive points. Yan immediately retaliated, scoring seven points. After that, the back-and-forth was intense, and it was difficult to tell who would win. When the score reached a 16-16 tie, Sun suddenly committed frequent errors, repeatedly missing opportunities, resulting in a 16-21 loss in the first set. In the second set, Sun rallied and launched a strong counterattack, using half-volley shots to defeat the enemy. However, the opponent's strategy was the same, so the scores were always within two points of each other. After a fierce battle, Sun won back a set with a score of 12-19. The third set was for the championship title, so both players were extremely cautious. Yan fought with all his might, and Sun also tried hard to keep up. At 12-11, Yan suddenly scored six consecutive points with low-angle shots. At this point, Sun was exhausted and unable to catch up. Although he had several good plays, they were of no avail. Yan won with a score of 22-25, thus winning this year's championship.

Director Pan's Speech: The Relationship Between Physical Education and Hygiene Education at the Municipal Physical Education College 158

Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau of this city, was invited by the Municipal Physical Education College on the 9th of this month to attend the weekly memorial service for the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen at the school and give a speech. The topic of his speech was "The Relationship Between Physical Education and Hygiene Education." The original text is as follows:

Distinguished teachers, dear students, today I am here to attend the Municipal Physical Education College's weekly memorial service for the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen. It can be said that this is my first time visiting the school and speaking to you all. At the same time, I am very happy to see that the school is in good spirits.

Under the leadership of Mayor Wu, our municipal government has been unanimously promoting and encouraging national physical education, especially among young people. This year, the performance of our country's delegation at the World Games was poor because our physical strength could not compete with others, resulting in our lagging far behind in all sports. Everyone felt very ashamed. At the same time, we believe that if the physical fitness of the general public in such a large country is improved, we will naturally occupy a place in international sports competitions. Therefore, the mayor made a grand wish to establish a Shanghai Municipal Physical Education College, intending to build it into a relatively perfect and ideal physical education school in the country, to cultivate physical education talents, to train physical education teachers, and to promote and accelerate the development of general physical education in the country. You must all have long understood the fundamental meaning of establishing this school.

What I want to talk about today is the relationship between physical education and hygiene education.

Our promotion of physical education is not only focused on sports and the progress of competition results, but fundamentally on improving the physical strength and prolonging the lifespan of the general public, so that they can shoulder more burdensome work and do more things to seek happiness for the entire country and nation. If we first pay attention to the achievements of athletes, then at best, we will only cultivate a very small number of athletes, and the majority of the people will still not have healthy bodies. What help is that to the entire nation? Moreover, if the general physical fitness of the people does not meet the standard, it is a dream to have outstanding athletes who can compete with other countries. The current situation in our country is that the physical strength of the general public is not as good as that of others. Therefore, there are fewer people who can shoulder work than others, which has led to the state of being called the "sick man of East Asia." In the midst of such serious national difficulties, each of us should do the work of two people, and the work of one day should be equivalent to the work of two days. To achieve this goal, we must all promote physical education, hoping that every member of the entire nation will have a healthy physique to shoulder extraordinary work. At the same time, if the standard of physical strength can be developed to above the international level, then we can naturally win a considerable position in the competition, without having to force it.

I always have a feeling that physical education is a part of hygiene education—that is, health education. Physical education and hygiene are truly inseparable.

Speaking of physical education methods and types of sports, I am a complete layman. However, from an educational point of view, there seem to be many areas that are worth studying. In the future, you will be responsible for training central school students. You must study their physical strength, temperament, and personality separately, and you cannot stick to rigid methods. You must know that the purpose of physical education is to make people healthier from unhealthy, and less sick from sick. If the method is not suitable, and you force it to be implemented in a rigid way, in fact, while some people can achieve considerable progress, perhaps others will not only not progress because they exceed the limit, but also affect their physical health. I hope that comrades engaged in physical education will not only examine it from the practical perspective, but also work hard from the research perspective. Do not think that various methods and projects are always "what others have, I have," and "what others say, I say," without being willing to conduct any research. The Municipal Physical Education College should adopt a research and experimental attitude, and use methods and equipment to improve ourselves. Use good methods and improve bad ones in order to test out a training program that is suitable for the needs of the whole country to increase the efficiency of progress. (To be continued)

The yarn market is rising sharply with good momentum. Although the yarn sales market is still mediocre, buyers' intentions are very strong. Some are slightly throwing out when prices rise due to the rampant banditry in Suiyuan.

Spot goods for unbleached cotton cloth were the most scarce. Eastern goods, fine cloth, and fine twill were not selling as well. Although the output of local factories was high, there was still a shortage of supply due to the continued strong demand from the Yangtze River gang and the dyeing factory inland gang. Market prices also rose by about five fen to one jiao (per piece). Fine cloth from Chinese factories was gradually increasing production again, but the selling price was no less expensive than that of Eastern goods. White twill and flannel had once softened a week ago, but recently, due to the scarcity of spot goods, the market trend suddenly became expensive again. Printed flannel, blue cloth, coarse cloth, and other goods were uniformly firm. Actual sales were gradually expanding, with the Yangtze River and Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces being the most prominent. Due to the approaching sales season, the prices of lower-grade thick cloth have risen sharply, so each factory has gradually decided to raise prices. The market situation for the day is recorded below.

The closing price was 1,155.5 yuan. Yuan Mao, Yongda, Decheng, Tongfeng, Henglai entered, rising to 5.7 yuan. Hongchang, Yongyuan Mao, Yongdingkang, Wanxing sold out, gradually falling to 5.1 yuan. Qia Yongdingkang took advantage of the low to enter, rebounding to 5.6 yuan. The closing price was 1,155.5 yuan.

The standard price of auction gold announced by the Central Bank was 1,156.8 yuan. According to the closing price, it was about 1 yuan more. The amount registered in November was 1,153 yuan, and in January it was 1,155 yuan. The water supplement in the morning was 1,152 yuan. The price of red gold was 5 yuan more, at 1,160.6 yuan. The spot market was stable. Tianjin goods were 11.5 yuan more. The buying price of cooked red was 8 yuan, and the selling price was 13.5 yuan. There were no transactions. The swap spread was about 1.8 yuan paid out by the longs.

There were not many transactions in the market. In summary, Wanxing and Dada Decheng Yiyu were on the buyer's side, and Tongfeng Hengyuan Gai, Yong Qia, Feng, Yongcheng Da Shen, and Da Yongshengyuan Yonghongchang were on the seller's side. Wanxing Qiafeng Yong advanced and then exited, and Yuanfa Yongtongfeng Heng Dada Decheng exited first and then entered.

It was found that the market was peaceful throughout the day. The morning opening price was 1,155.6 yuan, and the closing price was 1,155.5 yuan. The highest price was 1,155.7 yuan, and the lowest price was 1,154.9 yuan. There were eight jiao fluctuations. As a result, it fell slightly by one jiao compared to the previous closing. There were 2,758 strips of December notes left, totaling five long companies and twenty-four short companies. There were 5,250 strips of January futures, totaling thirty-three long companies and fifteen short companies. The total number of transactions was 336 in the morning and 238 in the afternoon.

Although the Market Price of Hardware Zinc Sheets is High, the Listed Price Has Fallen 176

Zinc sheets are in short supply due to active procurement by battery factories, cigarette factories, and others, causing prices to rise several times a day. For example, No. 1 is priced at 145 yuan, No. 4 at 150 yuan, No. 5 and No. 6 at 155 yuan, and No. 7 at 138 yuan. Nos. 3 and 8, as well as thick patterned sheets, are selling more slowly, so prices remain between 130 and 140 yuan, showing no change. However, overseas listed prices eased by half a pound yesterday, selling at £19 15s per ton.

Concerns About the Future of the U.S. Dollar: Chinese Merchants Have Been Selling for Days 177

Yesterday's exchange market saw a slight rise in exchange rates. Although banks were bullish, Chinese merchants continued to sell, keeping the market stable. Early in the morning, overseas telegrams indicated that in London, both near and far term contracts showed a tendency towards increased supply after the market closed, with the price dropping below 0.0625, prompting short covering. The New York silver market remained unchanged. London forward silver prices fell by 4 to 7 points. London gold fell by one penny. Sterling rose 25 points against the U.S. dollar and 2 pounds against the French franc. The U.S. dollar rose 25 points against both sterling and the French franc. The Central Bank's official rates were announced, with both sterling and the U.S. dollar remaining stable. The Customs Gold Unit remained unchanged. At the opening of the exchange market in the morning, the near-term selling price for sterling was 1 shilling, 2 pence, 5/625, and for the U.S. dollar, it was 19.625 and 6875, a slight increase compared to the previous close, indicating stability for both sterling and the U.S. dollar. After the opening, Chinese merchants continued to liquidate their positions, while Japanese banks sold East Asian currencies. HSBC's official rates were announced, with both sterling and the U.S. dollar remaining stable. Although banks were bullish, the market remained stable. Later, after the announcement of the silver equalization tax reduction by half, the banks' appetite for supply remained uneven. Japanese banks engaged in arbitrage, selling sterling and buying the U.S. dollar. Throughout the process, the market fluctuated. Later in the day, Chinese merchants again sold U.S. dollars, which foreign banks worked hard to maintain, keeping the overall trend stable. The Indian silver report showed a decrease of seven annas, but ultimately remained unchanged. By the close of trading, the near-term selling price for sterling was 1 shilling, 2 pence, 5615, and for the U.S. dollar, it was 29.62 and 6875, indicating a balanced supply of both near and far-term contracts for sterling and the U.S. dollar compared to the previous close. Chinese merchants continued to sell U.S. dollars, while banks remained bullish. Shanghai, however, bought U.S. dollars. The trading record for today is as follows:

The opening near-term selling price for sterling was 1 shilling, 2 pence, 5625. Banque Belge bought spot at 9375. Holland China Trading Company bought January at 5315. Jardine Matheson bought spot at 59375. (Arbitrage between sterling and Japanese yen was 1 shilling, 2 pence, and 32/1). The afternoon near-term selling price was 1 shilling, 2 pence, 5625. Later, HSBC bought January at 9325. Silk and Tea: Unprecedented Prosperity in the Silk Market; Price Fluctuations Inevitable 178

Yesterday, silk trading in Shanghai suddenly experienced extraordinary activity, leading to some market volatility. Initially, due to slight weakness in overseas silk prices the previous day, local sentiment feared a retracement after the surge. Consequently, manufacturers telegraphed offers to sell abroad in large quantities, but at prices that were not excessively high, bringing the buying and selling prices fairly close. Furthermore, as of yesterday morning, actual sales in the silk markets of Japan and the United States improved, and silk prices rose sharply (New York spot prices rose by 6 cents, and futures rose by 7.5 cents, averaging approximately 29 yuan per picul in Shanghai; Yokohama spot prices rose to the 900 yuan mark, and futures also rose by 24 yuan). As a result, silk offers were telegraphed and sold as expected. At the same time, Western merchants also absorbed silk strongly, leading to brisk sales. A total of 1,114 bales were traded today. Unfortunately, market prices were not very uniform. Looking at silk prices in Shanghai, the 20 yuan decline from the previous day has already been recovered yesterday, and even surpassed. Yesterday, only 15 bales of User silk were traded. However, the total domestic and foreign silk sales throughout the day can be described as unprecedented this year, which was also quite unexpected.

Reading the Script of "Sai Jinhua" 180

— Chu Yang

I enjoy watching plays, but I'm not particularly fond of reading scripts. In my opinion, it's best to let the concrete images and actions unfold on the stage, which is more interesting and makes more sense. Although there are some plays in literary history that are both interesting and make sense, they are never performed. However, I believe the success of a play should be determined by "the effect of the performance." This evaluation is best based on the play's impact and resonance with the audience. Some may argue that "civilized plays" appeal to certain audiences, making them cheer and applaud. How should we evaluate these plays? In fact, the impact of "civilized plays" on audiences, regardless of their social class, is objectively negative. Xia Yan's play "Sai Jinhua" has already been staged. In preparation for seeing the play, I read the script. I should have read this script earlier, as it had already sparked heated debate in the theatrical and literary circles.

Using the historical Boxer Rebellion as a subject for a play is worthwhile. "Sai Jinhua" is an extremely dramatic figure, making her a compelling protagonist. Some have questioned whether the author focuses on the Boxer Rebellion or on Sai Jinhua herself. Some believe that the theme is not clear. I believe the theme is neither exclusively the former nor the latter, and it doesn't seem to have "two themes." If the Boxer Rebellion were the theme, the development of the historical events of the Boxer Rebellion would have to be the focus, showing its causes, consequences, and significance. The protagonist could not be "a girl from this troupe," even if she "shook the hand of Empress Frederick" (as stated in the play) and "slept with German Field Marshal Waldersee for some time" (as stated by Lu Xun). If the latter were the theme, the tragedy of this woman in the play is not developed to its full potential, and historical events and figures are interspersed and float to the surface. So, is this play a social history drama or a personal tragedy? The author's own answer is the most appropriate: "a satirical historical drama." He aims to "depict a gallery of portraits of lackeys set against the backdrop of the Boxer Rebellion, attempting to place everyone from Sai Jinhua to Wei Bangxian within the focal point of the narrative." The author's main target is the betrayers of China. Because he lived in a besieged city in northern China for two months, hearing stories about the chaos of thirty-seven years ago, he was reminded of the current situation. "So he wanted to expose the ugliness of the betrayers and awaken public awareness of 'national defense within our borders.' He used the figures of those who were active in this besieged city and transposed them onto figures from around the time of the Boxer Rebellion to write a play of a satirical nature" (Xia Yan, "A Letter to the Performers," published in the inaugural issue of "Literary Circle"). This is the author's stated motivation for writing the play. Although the play does not directly address "national defense within our borders," it does indeed use the ugly behavior and shameless acts of treason of the betrayers of China during the Boxer Rebellion to satirize the reality of the present. Therefore, we can define the theme of the play as: using historical satire to oppose national betrayal. I believe this is the correct interpretation of the author's intention, and the play's "national defense" significance lies therein.

The most superficial misinterpretation is to regard Sai Jinhua as a national hero, a great historical figure, a patriot, and a benefactor of the people of Beijing. No wonder Lu Xun's last testament did not forget to satirize: "Drama has already found its 'most central theme': even Sai Jinhua, who slept with the German Field Marshal Waldersee during the Boxer Rebellion, has long been canonized as the Nine Heavens Protector Goddess" (see "This Is Also Life" in the inaugural issue of "Zhongliu"). Lu Xun was satirizing those who regarded Sai Jinhua as the "Nine Heavens Protector Goddess," and clearly not the author, because the author's "most central theme" was not to praise Sai Jinhua, but to oppose the betrayers. He did not portray the female protagonist as a "national hero," but explicitly wrote about a woman who "used her body to win the enemy's favor and prolong her life in a chaotic world." However, she retained more humanity than those "who sat high in the halls of power, scowling at their compatriots but groveling before the enemy." Therefore, he "only wanted to portray her as an ordinary woman, commonly seen in China then and now, containing all the weaknesses common to all women. To depict her character as truthfully as possible, hoping to show that she merely played a role in this tragic era due to a chance opportunity" (quoted from Xia Yan's letter above). The sympathy the author has for her is something his female protagonist may not understand. Old Sai Jinhua might think the great master who gave her ten yuan was sympathizing with her.

Understanding Sai Jinhua in this way does not diminish this "Guanyin who saved thousands upon thousands of lives with a single word!" Regarding the significance of historical figures, we should, along with the playwright, grasp the authenticity of his protagonist (is it not enough? Or is it exaggerated?). We may as well sympathize with her, but certainly not treat her as the "Nine Heavens Protector Goddess," like the people of Beijing did thirty-seven years ago. We should see Sai Jinhua as the center of historical satire. "In times of great national upheaval, it is not the high-ranking officials who can truly speak for the people, but a beautiful young woman like her!" (as stated in the play). This is enough satire of the incompetence of the Qing officials! The fact that things that "High Minister" cannot handle rely on Sai Jinhua selling a little face to foreigners exhausts the artistry of satire.

The script of "Sai Jinhua" is not without its flaws. Although I don't understand playwriting and theatrical techniques, I feel that the development of the plot and the flow of scenes are not very good. The scenes are too scattered, and the tone of the play lacks unity. Perhaps it would be better adapted into a movie. This remains to be seen depending on the success of the performance. The definitive thing is that the personalities of the characters other than the protagonist and two or three others (Li Hongzhang, Sun Jiading, Wei Bangxian) are too cartoonish (Waldersee is also the same). This can be supplemented somewhat if the director directs well during the performance. As for the "Boxers" reflected in the play, only the bad and violent aspects are written, while the expression of the just and anti-imperialist feelings of the Chinese people at that time is ignored. This shows the author's lack of a deeper understanding and expression of historical truth. Overall, although the historical significance of this play is not as great as "The Initial European Flag" and "Roar, China!", and the satirical significance is not as perfect and fully integrated throughout the play as Gogol's "The Inspector General," it is still a powerful work in Chinese playwriting. It is still an initial achievement in both historical and satirical drama, and no one can deny that it deserves a considerable evaluation in the realm of national defense drama.

For the Sake of the Motherland 181

— Tian Jian

For the sake of the motherland,

Let us die,

Let us fight!

Our souls,

Have already risen,

Ready to sacrifice.

Let our blood,

Bathe—

Dreamlike fields,

Rivers,

Forests.

We have no freedom,

Freedom awaits us,

Freedom,

Freedom, ah,

On the battlefield—

For the sake of the motherland,

Let us die,

Embrace the flames of the earth.

We died,

We also triumphed...

Reading with Diligence · Miscellaneous Notes on O'Neill's Dramas 182

— Yu

Leap year, presidential election year, November 1936. Franklin Roosevelt was once again propelled by the voters onto the White House, a monarch without a dynasty but with a limited term, all due to diligence. Eugene O'Neill was also awarded the Nobel Prize in Literature, a combination of fame and fortune, by the Nobel Prize Committee later in the same month. (Perhaps the reason for awarding him the Nobel Prize this time is not the same as the reason for awarding it to Bunin in the previous two years, because O'Neill was able to maintain the old American style.) November 1936 was an unusual month and an unusual year for easily moved Americans (or, to be more fashionable and widely known, Yankees), perhaps a page of unusual historical facts that Yankee historians apprenticing now will write in the future. From a personal point of view, my skin is not white enough, and I am not qualified to be a wealthy American retiree. From a professional standpoint, I would rather have the lame Roosevelt elected than the copper-smelling puppet Landon take the stage. But this major event that could be a newspaper headline, newspaper material, has already passed. Four years ago, after the election results were revealed late at night, I wrote all night for the election of this lame president, but now I have no such interest or need. I am already satisfied after reading the newspaper headlines, and I am proud of this American playwright who won the Nobel Prize, because I have a certain fondness for his plays and at the same time only a smattering of knowledge about them. In this country, learned literary authorities may not have enough time, or perhaps because of what Lu Xun (may he rest in peace) said, they shy away from "work that requires a lot of effort but yields little profit." The power is then entrusted to us "small soldiers to wear the marshal's seal."

I am not a drama critic, not a playwright, not a director, not an actor, and certainly not an authority on O'Neill studies in China. I also have no experience in stagecraft, but I am just a professional writer with an empty stomach (because calling myself a "literary man" is a bit of an exaggeration). What can I say? What can I quote? What can I copy? It's truly like "lifting a stone to crush one's own foot"! But I can't control so much. Let's rack my brains.

Many years ago, in a so-called highest institution of learning infested with parasites who made a living by selling knowledge at heavily discounted prices, some young people gathered together and learned from a classmate who is now a famous playwright about O'Neill, an American playwright who had recently climbed to the highest honor, as told by a certain professor. At the same time, they learned that one of his plays was called "The Emperor Jones." Although I didn't study liberal arts, I was somewhat greedy for literature books. I stole time to read "The Emperor Jones," but unexpectedly, the American slang used by the black characters in it was beyond my ability to understand. Even if I did understand, it would take a lot of effort, so I gave up on this "royal book." Later, when I worked as a "jack-of-all-trades" helping with writing, I had a few American magazines to read and a few literary books to consult. American critics often talked about O'Neill, praised O'Neill, and were proud of O'Neill. I began to pay attention to this red-hot figure in the American literary world, who was imbued with the mysterious atmosphere of Ireland and wallowed in Freudian theory. From those comments that talked about him, praised him, and were proud of him, I learned that he had once been a sailor, and many of his plays had many scenes depicting the beauty of the sea. Some romantic ideals left to me by the petty bourgeoisie then turned into a dreamer of the sea, an admirer of sailors, a worshiper of pirates, and an enthusiastic lover of marine literature. I love Stevenson, I love Loti, I love certain works of Ibanez, I love all of Conrad's novels (although in "Typhoon," Chinese coolies were often treated like beasts, and I once got angry and threw the novel away). I also loved O'Neill. But although I was dreaming, dreaming of the sea, I couldn't be like "young Harry, the character in Conrad's short story 'Tomorrow'," and never "rot in one place," nor did I "take the world as my home." As a result, I finally became "Robert Mayo" in O'Neill's play "Beyond the Horizon," dreaming all day long, pointing to the beyond, summoned by the beauty, the distant and unknown beauty, yearning for the bewitching mystery, in order to let my unrestrained spirit roam in the vast space and wander freely, in pursuit of the joy of the secret hidden in that beyond. (The above quotations are based on Xu Youcheng's translation of "Beyond the Horizon"). But what was the result? He "married the soil" in order to win the love of the girl Ruth, working on that "stingy" soil, and shortened his life. This is the ruthless reality, and this is the unattainable and un-courageous fantasy of the Philistine. A young lad may have the courage of a Bohemian, a middle-aged person who is not too old and not too worldly may still have the fantasies of a Bohemian, but an old person, with rare exceptions, even this kind of fantasy has been completely worn away in the burdens of life. I used to be in the home of a professor whom I looked down upon, and he seemed to intentionally or unintentionally hint to me, "Little boy, are you restless? Do you have all sorts of ideals? I tell you, once you get married, once you get older, you will be as tame as a sheep. I think the best way to deal with those troublemaking young people is just to find them a partner." After listening to his words, I remember arguing with a red face, and the result was an unhappy breakup. A few years have passed, and I am not old yet. What does the reality tell us? I am savoring the professor's words and feeling a chill. This may be the reason why I was somewhat moved when I read O'Neill's play "Beyond the Horizon." Now, don't let that kind of Bohemian fantasy be lost again. When you have not experienced something, or eagerly hope for something, perhaps the color and flavor of that kind of emotion is different. We who have married the soil may envy the freedom of the sea, while "sailors who sail like horses" may yearn for the kind of stagnant, stinking family life on land that we have. "Old Harry" in "Tomorrow" became a sailor, but he was very disgusted with sailors. In Conrad's autobiographical novel "Youth," he also expressed his weariness with that sea life. Reading O'Neill's "Anna Christie," the father "Chris Christopherson" hated sea life. He hated the constant hard work at sea. He thought it was not good to seek a life at sea. His family members were all sailors. What was their life like? They only got rich wages in their pockets, got drunk, were robbed, and were penniless, and then went sailing again. They didn't go home. They didn't do anything a good person would do. "That old devil sea" would eventually swallow up his family members one day. So he hoped that his daughter Anna, according to his ideal, would one day "marry a good, stable land-dwelling fellow in the eastern United States, have her own home, have a few children, and he could be a grandfather, and he could go see them every time he came ashore." (See Anna Christie by Boni and Liverright, New York). This is the idea of an old sailor. Young sailors may not dream of settling down on land. In O'Neill's other play, "The Hairy Ape," the protagonist of the book, "Yank," who is called the hairy ape, hears the song of his companions:

"In far Canada,

Across the far sea,

There is a girl who is waiting passionately,

Organizing a family for me."

Then, this Mr. Hairy Ape Yank spoke with extreme contempt: "Stop farting, you lowly insects! Where did you get that phony family, family, hell! I'll organize a family for you! I'm going to beat you to death. Family! Tell family to go to hell! Where did you get that phony? This is home, understand? What do you want a home for? (Proudly) I ran away from my family when I was a child. Glad to be victorious, that's me. Family is a punishment for me, all in all. But you can't bet your shirts with me, none of you can do anything to me later. Want to try, any of you? Ha, I despise you. (In a more compromise but still contemptuous tone) (Girls waiting for you. Ha? Damn hell! That's all phony. They're not waiting for anyone. They're tricking you out of money. They're all whores, what words do you have to refute me? Treat them roughly, that's me. Tell them to go to hell! Whores, that's the whole thing, all of them." This sailor Yank looks down on women and looks down on family. What is it about the sea that attracts him? Perhaps as his companion Paddy said: When the ship opened "all the sails, countless days and nights," "the sky is burning like fire, the stars are twinkling eyes." On moonlit nights, you see the ship passing through the dim night, the sails of the ship are hoisted high, everything is covered with silvery white, and there is not a sound on the deck. Many of us dream, waiting all the time, until the ship you are on seems as if it is not a real ship at all, but a ghost ship like the Flying Dutchman. They say that ship will float on the sea forever without relying on the harbor." And in the daytime, "the warm sun shines on the clean deck. The sun warms your blood, and the sea breeze blowing in from the distant, dazzling, emerald-green ocean touches your lungs like strong wine." This kind of attraction of the sea is indeed enough to make us, who are rotting on land and at most creeping miserable creatures, dream of the ocean.

Yes, the ocean is worth lingering in, and the dream of the ocean will also attract people to do it. Once, I heard a friend of about the same age as me say that when he was a student, he wanted to escape from that uniquely Chinese dead family, put on a sailor's clothes, wore a sailor's white hat, and traveled back and forth on the deck, encountering a life with the sea as his home. My heart jumped. This remark seemed to come from the bottom of my heart. I think this kind of fantasy is probably common to all of us young boys and girls. I once read a story in the "North American Magazine" published in the United States about a British college student who became a pirate, and I was very fascinated. Destroying the Confucian robe and jumping out of this literary hell filled with the breath of death, what could be more romantic than this? But the dreams have long been blown away by the cold of the west wind. Now is not the time for us to dream. This kind of dream may be harmful to ourselves and our times. To borrow O'Neill's words: "Romantic fantasies, they have destroyed more lives than disease." (See his long play "Strange Interlude.") Our times do not allow us to dream anymore. We still have meaningful things waiting for us to do. Look: We have thousands of heavy stones on our heads; look, we are treading on an abyss-like pit; look, the waters of the Pacific are overflowing with bloodshed; look, the shameless are offering our鲜red blood with the most shameless means; look, the sick are drawing our path to death in the most sick posture; look, international hooligans are setting traps for us with the most sinister plans and the most solid chains, calling us to walk into their traps; look, there are no fences for iron hooves; look, there are no fences for spear points; look, there are no fences for the rampant airplanes; look, there are no fences for the intrusion of smuggled goods; look, there are no fences for the import of poisons; look, there are no fences for the internal crimes of the puppet army. Romantic fantasies, I want to borrow the title of a long novel by the British novelist Robert Graves to say for me: "Goodbye to All That."

Xi'an, the Historical City with Rusty Traces 183

— Hu Yifan

Xi'an, this historical city with rusty traces, is truly soaked in ancient charm all over.

For example, as soon as you walk out of the street, what greets your eyes is the Bell Tower, which distinguishes the east, west, north, and south streets, standing like a giant in the center of the avenue, right? This majestic and huge building, accompanied by the Drum Tower, which is less than half a mile away to the north and has the same heroic appearance, stands facing each other there, and they have been boasting for several centuries.

So, if you like to commemorate the past, then there are enough places for you to ponder, and you have to linger everywhere. A barren open space is the ruins of some king or marquis, and a weathered stele is the handwriting of some talented scholar or celebrity. There is Du Fu Alley, and somewhere else is the Qin King's Mansion. Where is the Yin'an Hall, and where is the Imperial Garden? Everywhere, everything everywhere, is filled with ancient scenery, ancient relics, and sentiments, making you sigh, making you gasp, making you feel overwhelmed by the past and present. Those with deep ancient feelings will even shed tears!

So, you change your mind: from commemorating the past to viewing the existing. You go to the magnificent and solemn Confucian Temple in the south of the city. There, you can see the rare thousand-year-old pines and cypresses in the northwest, standing tall in the open space in front of the halls. There are also the towering, huge rectangular stone tablets, which are also precious rubbings of inscriptions from ancient times. After circling the halls, you climb the red steps and can see the majestic main hall, the magnificent glazed tiles, the huge pillars, the beautiful oil paintings, and the clean corridors. When you recite:

"The Place of the Great Accomplisher, Most Sage, First Teacher Confucius," even if you are the children of the Western God, after seeing that kind of solemn and pure artistic conception, you cannot but silently show respect.

Going to the Stele Forest next door is even more "an ancient forest indeed." It is said that it contains the essence of our nation's culture for thousands of years. No wonder the newspaper reported that the government recently decided to spend 50,000 yuan to renovate it.

There, there is no scenery of any kind. What there is is horizontal and vertical, a pile here and a pile there, lining up tens of thousands of stone tablets of all sizes. What Wei stele characters, written by Emperor Taizong of Tang, written by Kangxi and Qianlong, "imperial brushes" of emperors and cats and dogs of all dynasties, are all there. There are also many painting posts (of course, those of Wu Daozi are even more numerous). In short, it is worthy of being the source of Chinese rubbings. Outsiders (like the author) will naturally become dizzy and dazzled when they walk in to take a quick look. Even those who are in the know, when they get inside, will probably inevitably study and appreciate until they are exhausted.

You cannot but go to the History Museum (inside the current Provincial Library). Entering there, it is even more filled with strange things you have never seen or heard of on weekdays. A few broken stone slabs are put together, and it tells you that this is the Six Steeds of the Tang Dynasty (note). A dark, lacquer-black stove that villagers use to burn incense is a Zhou bronze tripod or Shang bronze ritual vessel from thousands of years ago. A stone bodhisattva with a muddy face, broken hands, and broken feet is a stone carving from the Jin and Wei dynasties. Small to the point of a broken bowl is cloisonné, and a tar-black copper piece is a Xin Mang currency. Gathered inside are bricks, tiles, Jesus, what the Weiyang Palace is, and the Afang Palace. In short, everything here is old and tells you about ancient years and ancient civilizations. As soon as you enter there, you will unconsciously come out with a body full of "ancient air."

After walking through these places, regardless of whether you will become a connoisseur or not, you have at least received the baptism of "ancient." So, when you walk into an antique shop, you will not be surprised by the fact that a newly unearthed broken tile and remnant brick is priced at forty or fifty yuan. When you walk into a restaurant and see ancient characters and books hanging on the wall, and ancient mirrors and bottles displayed on the table, you will feel that it is not appropriate and out of tune.

So, from ordinary people's homes, whether it is on a table or a pit, on a wall or a chair, you can always find one or two ancient utensils or ancient toys. Perhaps, from under a very dark opium lamp, you will discover an ancient Jiajing plate.

So, although airplanes are flying all over the sky and cars are running all over the streets, you may instead dream of the leisurely demeanor of the wooden oxen and flowing horses of ancient times. Your ears have also become "ancient." After listening to Western music, you will love Qin opera again. Your taste has also become "ancient." You will hate big dishes and seasonal dishes and love steamed buns and soup. As soon as the sky is light, you are already sitting at the restaurant that is said to have a pot head with a history of several hundred years.

So, in your own inn, although your furnishings have three-dimensional furniture, table golf, and a radio, you still need ancient Buddhas and ancient bottles. Those with more refined taste will also need Qin bricks, Han tiles, Wei steles, and Jin rubbings.

Slowly, the ancient charm of the city has been collected by you, so you can walk to the suburbs at will.

The suburbs are also full of ancient charm. East, south, west, and north, which place is not full of ancient charm and ancient sites?

Want to climb high? You can go to Mount Hua if it is far away, and you can climb Mount Zhongnan if it is near. It is a scenic spot for immortals, with pleasant scenery. Want to see the water? You can go to Guanzhong, observe the Yellow River, and watch the Xiaoshui River. It is also a famous ancient giant stream in the world. Want to pay homage to the great dead? There is the Yellow Emperor in中部, Emperor Taizong of Tang in Xianyang, and Emperor Qin in Lintong. Want to bathe and swear allegiance to your lover? You can take your Western-dressed Xi Shi or yellow-faced wife out of Lintong to the east. The Huaqing Pool is exactly the scenic spot and famous area where Li Sanlang and Ah Huan have been romantic for thousands of years. If you are still more affectionate, you might as well hold hands and go to Mawei Slope in Xingping to commemorate the burial place of this beautiful woman who has disappeared for thousands of years. Well, Ah... the heroic spirit underground will also be grateful if it knows.

In addition, such as the world-famous "Wang Baochuan", which has been studied in London and also performed, the ancient site is located in "Wujiapo," which is only ten miles away from Xi'an. There is also the Ba River, which now goes without saying that the riverbed is facing the sky, but it used to be the heartbreaking place for poets who bid farewell at the Ten Mile Pavilion. There are also the ruins of the ancient Wei'an city, the vast and majestic earth mounds, which will make people think of the atmosphere and greatness of the imperial capital in the past. There is also that... there is also that... In short, the famous scenic spots and historical sites of Xi'an are inexhaustible to write about and inexhaustible to play with. The whole of Xi'an is shrouded in an atmosphere of "ancient." All the residents of Xi'an are completely enclosed in this atmosphere.

But what is a bit of a pity is that those who can breathe and appreciate this ancient charm are not the people of Xi'an who created the ancient sites in the past and are still creating them now, but rather some people who have nothing to do with it at all—so, no wonder the ancient Xi'an has recently become a bit dim. When Mr. Lu Yan wrote his impression of Xi'an last year, he only wrote about opium and crows and missed "ancient charm," or perhaps that is the reason.

(Note: The Six Steeds are said to be the stone carvings of the images of the six precious horses of Emperor Taizong of Tang who died for commemorating his risking arrows and stones and carrying heavy wounds.)

Expressing My Deep Condolences to the Chinese People 184

— Takeuchi Ketsuro

When I read about Lu Xun's death in the newspaper, I, like all revolutionary Japanese, felt great sorrow. Lu Xun's death is a great loss to the Chinese people, especially now, when the Chinese people desperately need their spokesperson. Lu Xun's death is also a great loss to the Japanese people, because through him we can hear the voices of the people in the neighboring country.

Truly, he is the greatest writer in the East. Just like every great writer, he is also a great thinker. He dedicated all his talents and knowledge to the liberation of the Chinese people. Unfortunately, the Japanese people do not yet have such a great and influential writer as our spokesperson. Our Japanese revolutionary literature should learn more from Lu Xun's literary legacy.

After the death of Gorky, world literature lost another of its great representatives. I would like to express my deep condolences to the Chinese people through you. (Translated by Lai Shi)

Mr. Takeuchi is a member of the Japanese "Literary Guidance Society." The above paragraph is translated from a private letter he gave me. The original text is in Esperanto. ——Translator

The Road to Health

— Edited by Kangjian Pharmaceutical Society

The Latest Invention in the Treatment of Gonorrhea: The Supreme and Great Strategy Longed for by All Humanity 185

— Original text from Far Eastern Medical Journal No. 34, translated by Yang Daonan, graduate of the Russian Labor Medical University

…An unheard-of method of treating gonorrhea with bile substances, achieving rapid and extraordinary results with extremely nimble procedures… Dr.'s thesis shocks the entire European medical community and proposes a simple external treatment for gonorrhea.

The biggest issue in venereology should be gonorrhea. In the past, there was no effective treatment for gonorrhea, a fact well-known by both the medical and non-medical communities. Precisely because there was no effective treatment, numerous remedies were constantly being introduced. However, these preparations mainly used yellow pigment as their primary component, and the quality of the yellow pigment was so poor that it often caused damage to the stomach and intestines and stimulated the kidneys. As for efficacy, yellow pigment only had diuretic and anti-inflammatory functions.
